Our Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Responsible Person Answers the Statement of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Saying That If There Are Any Illegal Actions Within Our Territory, We Absolutely Will Not Allow Them and Will Surely Find Ways to Eliminate Them

(Nanjing) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a statement on December 10 in the name of its spokesperson regarding the current Sino-Japanese negotiations. A reporter visited the responsible person of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the eleventh, and the following is a record of the conversation. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a statement on the tenth regarding the Sino-Japanese negotiations. I wonder how the Ministry of Foreign Affairs views this, and whether it is prepared to issue another statement. (Answered) The Ministry has already issued a statement on the seventh of this month regarding its attitude towards the Sino-Japanese negotiations, and has fully explained the sections that we should declare. There is no need to issue another statement, and it does not seem to have much meaning to repeatedly issue statements before the negotiations are concluded. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' statement mentioned that China and Japan are in complete agreement on three points: hiring Japanese advisors, cracking down on illegal Koreans, and reducing Chinese import taxes. What is the truth? (Answered) Our views on the above issues are still consistent with the news released by the Central News Agency on the seventh of this month. Please refer to that article to understand the truth. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' statement claimed that China has agreed to Japan to eradicate all anti-Japanese movements and revise anti-Japanese textbooks. What is the truth? (Answered) In past conversations, we have repeatedly stated frankly that our government has been doing its best to promote friendly relations and admonish the people. This has been our government's consistent policy. However, the emotions of the people arise naturally from the environment. The way to restore the people's feelings is to first eliminate the causes of animosity. Otherwise, even if the government strictly suppresses them, it may not achieve the results we desire. As for cracking down on anti-Japanese textbooks, we have pointed out that our country has no so-called anti-Japanese textbooks, and the Ministry of Education has a textbook review committee. Any textbook containing incorrect or insulting records, or comments that provoke international animosity, does not meet the set review standards. However, textbooks contain historical records, which are very legitimate and cannot be interfered with. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs stated that the memorandum left by Kawagoe records various issues that China has agreed to, and seems to be asking the Chinese government to implement them as soon as possible. What is our view? (Answered) Regarding the Kawagoe memorandum, the process has been recorded in various newspapers. The Japanese embassy calls this document a note verbale, which is a memorandum prepared unilaterally by the other party. We have formally declared to the Japanese side that this document cannot be used as a basis for reference, as many of the contents of the document do not match the previous negotiations. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs said that we have largely accepted the Japanese demands regarding the incidents that have occurred in various places. Is this true? (Answered) After the Chengdu incident occurred, the Ministry immediately advocated for a quick resolution in accordance with international conventions. Negotiations on a resolution are now beginning. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs said that after the Suiyuan issue occurred, we seemed to have an attitude of denying past conversations. Is this true? (Answered) We have not denied any of the sections discussed in the negotiations. However, while negotiations were underway, new situations that we were concerned about suddenly occurred, making it more difficult to conduct discussions. The issues discussed have not yet been concluded. (Reporter asked) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs said that if the lives and property of Japanese people in China are threatened, or if Japanese interests in China are infringed upon, the Japanese side will take necessary measures on the spot. What is our attitude towards this? (Answered) China has indeed not done anything to harm Japan's legitimate interests, and we should provide appropriate protection for the lives and property of Japanese people in accordance with international conventions. However, the Chinese government will not allow any foreign country to take any illegal actions within Chinese territory under any pretext, and will surely find ways to eliminate them. (Eleventh Central News Agency Telegram)

(Tokyo) A spokesman for the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs met with foreign journalists today and denied the Allied News Agency's report that the Japanese government has abandoned hope of resolving the issue with China through diplomatic channels. He said that the Japanese government still hopes to resolve various issues with China through diplomatic channels, as evidenced by the fact that the Japanese government has not yet recalled Ambassador Kawagoe. When asked why the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' statement yesterday did not mention China's reservations on various issues, the spokesperson replied that the Japanese statement was intended to declare Japan's views on the various issues that had been negotiated. The Chinese declaration expressed the views of the Chinese government, so there was no need to mention China's intentions in yesterday's statement. The spokesperson today acknowledged for the first time that the Japanese government has considered China's reservations, but said that Japan will never accept them. (Eleventh Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) After Kawagoe went to Shanghai, Suma and Gao Zongwu are discussing Sino-Japanese negotiations, such as the Chengdu incident. The two sides did not continue negotiations on the eleventh. It is heard that the trend of negotiations on the Chengdu incident is that it will not be difficult to resolve if it is handled in accordance with international conventions. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Japanese Deputy Consul in Beijing, Pura, visited Gao Zongwu at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the morning of the eleventh and had some discussions. (Eleventh Telegram)

Guangzhou "Nightlife" The Latest Situation: People Go to Bed Early and Get Up Early; Traffic Stops at Midnight

(Guangzhou) Guangzhou's "nightlife" has always been very prosperous and has contributed to the city's prosperity, but it no longer exists. Since the authorities implemented the New Life Movement, all theaters, entertainment venues, restaurants, tea houses, shops, etc. in the city must be closed by midnight. Thus, Guangzhou's entire nightlife has come to an end. Furthermore, since the authorities banned playing mahjong, all the restaurants and hotels in the city have been unusually quiet, and their business has been greatly affected. Recently, the police station has also prohibited people from walking or riding in cars through the streets after midnight. The New Life Committee has also ordered people to go to bed early and get up early, and public buses and other vehicles have also complied with the order to stop running after midnight. (Eleventh Reuters Telegram)

Tianjin Coal Prices Soar

(Tianjin) The coal shortage in Tianjin is getting worse, and prices have soared. The Social Affairs Bureau has sent personnel to investigate secretly, and those unscrupulous merchants who raise prices to hoard goods will be severely punished as a warning to others. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Remarks by Japanese Foreign Ministry Authorities: The Intention Lies in Addressing Domestic Concerns, There is No Immediate Tendency for Sino-Japanese Relations to Worsen, Awaiting China's Attitude Before Deciding on Countermeasures

(Tokyo) The Japanese Foreign Ministry issued a "Statement by Authorities" on the 10th, outlining the Japanese government's policy plan and opinions regarding Sino-Japanese negotiations. Although the meaning of the document seems important, the wording is quite cautious, and its purpose is to influence domestic opinion rather than to demonstrate power to China. No mention is made of the situation in China; only the points that both sides have supposedly already agreed upon are listed. The conclusion includes a phrase: "Japan will pay close attention to how China will crack down on anti-Japanese sentiment." The focus of the entire text can be seen in this sentence. The Allied Press published a table on the 10th showing the number of Japanese residents under the jurisdiction of Japanese consulates in China, which was published at the same time as the above document, which is obviously not without reason. According to general observations here, after the Chengdu, Beihai, and other incidents are resolved, the Japanese government seems to be waiting quietly for China's attitude before deciding on future policies. Therefore, the future of Sino-Japanese relations does not have an immediate tendency to worsen. Recently, there has been a growing sense among Japanese intellectuals that alleviating the rift between the peoples of China and Japan and enhancing goodwill is the most urgent task. Currently, many are seriously concerned about the signing of the Japan-Soviet Fisheries Agreement. If the Soviet Union continues to delay the signing of the agreement, Japan may take free action. The fishing season is approaching, starting in May next year. Under such circumstances, it is possible that Japan-Soviet relations will worsen. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Pingjin Paper Shortage

(Tianjin) There is currently a paper shortage in Pingjin, and newspapers are in severe lack. The price has risen from three yuan to more than five yuan and seven jiao, but there is still no stock. Fewer goods are coming from Canadian and Nordic paper mills, and demand exceeds supply. The companies that have recently transported goods have all delivered them to contract users. If the Suiyuan war expands and foreign paper is cut off, it will affect the North China news industry. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Tianjin Japanese Trust Company Established on New Year's Day

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Japanese Trust Company will be established on New Year's Day with a capital of five million, divided into 20,000 shares. The president is Akayama Imaasaji, which will be the only resource organization for Japanese industrial, commercial, and economic development in North China, not subject to the restrictions of the military or consulates. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Customs Officers Intercept Smuggled Goods in Tianjin Suburbs

(Tianjin) On the night of the 10th, three Korean smugglers from the Tianjin Japanese concession smuggling firm Gong Ji, including Cui Shangwu, used several heavy-duty trucks to transport 750 pieces of linen yarn, worth 6,000 yuan, intending to sell them in Gaoyang. They were intercepted by customs officers at Xiaoximen in the Tianjin suburbs. The smuggled goods were seized, and the three Koreans were extradited by the Japanese consulate on the 11th. The Japanese side protested to the customs, demanding their return, but was not allowed. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

The southward transport of smuggled goods by ronin has stopped since the 5th. The case of the eighteen confiscated trucks of smuggled goods is still being handled by Horiuchi, the chief consul, who is negotiating with the Shandong authorities for their return. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Legislative Yuan Passes Two Labor-Management Laws and Two Public Bond Ordinances

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 83rd meeting on the morning of the 11th. Sixty-eight members attended. The newly appointed Ling Bing, Zhang Ximan, Wen Yuanning, and Kou Kejing were among the first to arrive at the meeting. Sun Ke presided as chairman and Liang Hancao as secretary-general. Matters discussed: (1) The Labor Contract Law was resolved to continue reviewing each article in Chapter 2 of the law. It was passed after the second reading amendment based on the draft report and passed in its entirety, omitting the third reading. The law includes five chapters: General Provisions, Obligations of Workers, Obligations of Employers, Termination of Labor Contracts, Penalties, and Supplementary Provisions, totaling forty-three articles. The main points are that the terms of the labor contract shall be determined by the mutual agreement of the parties concerned. When a worker has the right of invention, the right of invention belongs to the worker. Labor remuneration has the right to claim first payment from the employer's property in the event of the employer's bankruptcy. (2) The Minimum Wage Law was resolved to pass with amendments based on the review report of the Labor Law Committee. The full text consists of twenty-three articles. The main points are that the minimum wage rate should be determined based on the local cost of living and the conditions of each industry, according to the following standards: A. The adult worker should be able to maintain himself and provide for the necessary living of two incapacitated relatives. B. The wages of child labor shall not be less than half of the minimum wage for adults. The minimum wage rate shall be determined by a minimum wage committee composed of both labor and management and the competent authority. Labor and management shall not enter into contracts with less than the minimum wage rate. The law may be implemented in different regions, and the regions shall be proposed by the Ministry of Industry and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. (Note: The purpose of the above two laws is to seek labor-management coordination and peace in the industry, which is urgently needed by all parties.) (3) Committee members Chuan Bingchang and others reported on the review and amendment of the names of the counties under the jurisdiction of the second, third, sixth, and tenth districts of the Guizhou Province listed in Appendix 2 of the National Assembly Representative Election Law. The resolution was passed according to the review report. (4) The Regulations on the Public Bonds of Jin Province in the Republic of China Year 26 and the Repayment and Interest Payment Table. (5) The Regulations on the Construction Public Bonds of the Jing-Gan Railway in the Republic of China Year 26 and the Repayment and Interest Payment Table. The resolution was passed according to the review reports of the Finance Committee. All other items on the agenda were postponed to the next meeting of the council due to time constraints. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

(Nanjing) The main points of the two public bond regulations passed by the Legislative Yuan on the 11th are as follows: (A) The Regulations on the Public Bonds of Jin Province in the 26th Year of the Republic of China consist of eleven articles. (1) The Jin Province Government will issue 10 million yuan of the Public Bonds of Jin Province in the 26th Year of the Republic of China on New Year's Day next year for the purpose of repaying the provincial bank's advances. (2) The interest rate is 7% per annum, and interest is paid twice a year on June 30 and December 31. (3) The repayment period is set at thirteen years. Interest is only paid in the first three years. The first repayment date is June 30, Year 29 of the Republic of China. The principal is repaid in ten years by lottery, with 500,000 yuan repaid every six months, and the entire amount is repaid by December 31, Year 38 of the Republic of China. The aforementioned lottery shall be held 20 days before each repayment date in the location of the provincial government, and personnel from the Ministry of Finance and the Auditing Department shall be dispatched to supervise. (4) The Jin Province land tax and the entire revenue from the provincial surtax are designated as the fund. The Jin Provincial Finance Department shall transfer the amount of principal and interest due each period as listed in the repayment and interest payment table in advance on a monthly basis to the account of the Public Bond Fund Management Committee of the Jin Province Bank for special storage and reserve payment. If it is insufficient, the amount shall be made up from the Jin Province land tax proper. The Public Bond Fund Management Committee shall be jointly organized by representatives from the Ministry of Finance, the Auditing Department, the Taiyuan Pacification Office, the Jin Province Government, the Jin Provincial Finance Department, the Jin Province Bank, and the Silver and Money Industry Association. Its organizational regulations shall be formulated by the Jin Province Government and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. (5) The bonds are divided into three types: 10,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 100 yuan. (6) The Jin Province Bank is the managing agency for the repayment of principal and interest of this public bond. (7) The bonds of this public bond are in bearer form and may be freely traded and mortgaged, and may be used as security deposits for official purposes. The winning bonds and expired interest coupons may be used to pay all taxes in Jin Province. (B) The Regulations on the Construction Public Bonds of the Jing-Gan Railway in the Republic of China Year 26 consist of thirteen articles. (1) The National Government will issue 14 million yuan of the Construction Public Bonds of the Jing-Gan Railway in the 26th Year of the Republic of China on New Year's Day next year by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways to extend the railway from Yicheng to Guixi. (2) The interest rate is 6% per annum, and interest is paid once every six months on June 30 and December 31. (3) The repayment period is set at ten years. The principal is repaid once every six months on June 30 and December 31 according to the amount specified in the repayment and interest payment table, and the entire amount is repaid by December 31, Year 35 of the Republic of China. The aforementioned repayment shall be made by lottery 20 days before each due date. (4) The following funds are designated for allocation: 1. The principal of the loan from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity that is being repaid from the 26th to the 35th year of the Republic of China under the contract signed by the Ministry of Railways and the board of directors managing the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity for the completion of the Yue-Han Railway. 2. The income after the Jing-Gan Railway starts operating. The aforementioned funds shall be transferred monthly by the Ministry of Railways according to the amount of principal and interest that should be repaid each period as stated in the repayment and interest payment table to the account of the Public Bond Fund Management Committee for special storage and reserve payment. If it is insufficient, it shall be supplemented by the Ministry of Railways. (5) The Public Bond Fund Management Committee shall be jointly organized by representatives from the Ministry of Finance, the Auditing Department, the board of directors managing the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity, and the bank managing this public bond, with two representatives from the Ministry of Railways. Its organizational regulations shall be formulated by the Ministry of Railways and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. (6) The matters concerning the repayment of principal and interest of this public bond shall be handled by the Public Bond Fund Management Committee, and the Central Bank is designated as the agency for paying the principal and interest. (7) This public bond shall be used exclusively for the purpose specified in Article 1 and shall not be used for other purposes. (8) The bonds are divided into two types: 1,000 yuan and 500 yuan. (9) This public bond is originally in bearer form and may be freely traded and mortgaged. When security deposits must be paid for official purposes, it may be used as a substitute and may also be used as a guarantee reserve for banks. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

(Nanjing) It is now known that the fundraising methods for the Jing-Gan Railway and the two public bonds of Jin Province have been successfully discussed with the banking sector. Of the 14 million yuan of construction public bonds for the Jing-Gan Railway, the Bank of Communications will underwrite 4 million yuan, the China Farmers Bank 3 million yuan, the Four Banks Savings Society 2.5 million yuan, and the China South Salt Industry, Jincheng, and Dalu Banks 1 million yuan each, and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank 500,000 yuan. The 10 million yuan of public bonds in Jin Province, because they are for repaying advances from the Jin Province Bank, will still be underwritten by the bank. Furthermore, the annual revenue from land taxes and provincial surcharges in Jin Province is more than 1.43 million yuan, which will definitely be sufficient to pay the principal and interest on the public bonds of Jin Province in the future. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 11th)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Importance of Recapturing Damiaozi

— Beginning

Since the overcoming of Bailingmiao, our army has played the second miracle in Suiyuan. The news of the capture of Damiaozi made the people feel a great revival again.

In terms of the military situation, the position of Damiaozi is very important. After losing Bailingmiao, Damiaozi became the most important military base for bandits and puppets. In this base, the remnants were reorganized and the strength was replenished. The bandits and puppets could attack Bailingmiao at any time. If Bailingmiao was shaken, it could further threaten Baotou, Guihua, and affect the overall situation in Suiyuan. Furthermore, if our army intends to make progress in eastern Suiyuan, it is essential to eliminate this hidden danger in northern Suiyuan. Without any worries in northern Suiyuan, our army can concentrate its forces and expand from eastern Suiyuan, realizing the plan to recover lost territory. In short, the recapture of Bailingmiao and Damiaozi showed special importance under the above circumstances, which completely eliminated the possibility of harassment in northern Suiyuan in a passive aspect, and opened up a new situation for promoting to eastern Suiyuan in a positive aspect.

In the recent victorious battle records of our army, we can get the following three revelations.

First, the recent victory has powerfully proved the mistake of "defeatism". Until recently, many people still doubted the strength of our army's resistance. This group of people believed that our army, whether in weapons or other equipment, was not enough to compare with the enemy, so it was difficult to win. However, the bandits and puppet troops who attacked me were supplied with military equipment and clothing by a certain party that instigated them, and there were also officers from a certain party directing the battle. As a result, our army actually won repeatedly and recovered important towns such as Bailingmiao and Damiaozi. The iron-like facts told us that our army has a very strong fighting force.

Second, from these two victories, we can see that our military should turn to a favorable trend—from passively resisting to actively recovering lost territory. Whether from a military technical point of view or other aspects, we can only gain victory by creating a factual advantage. Suppose that our army only guarded itself carefully against the enemy's attacks and did not actively capture important military bases such as Bailingmiao, perhaps northern and eastern Suiyuan would have been threatened many times more severely than they are now. Some people do not advocate any proactive military action, reasoning that it avoids the enemy's expanded entanglement. Little do they know that such a passive proposition, if applied, is precisely the root of the enemy's expanded entanglement. Only by initiating proactive actions can we cut off our current entanglements.

Third, from the fact that pseudo-bandits have defected one after another, we have gained a confirmation that is beneficial to our situation. People who observe the Suiyuan war with a pessimistic mindset often have a mistaken observation, thinking that pseudo-bandits and even the instigators behind them are a single harmonious entity. Taking the entire strength of their single entity to resist our partial resistance, naturally, there is only an ending of our defeat and their victory. They do not understand that pseudo-bandits and even the instigators behind them themselves have many contradictions and gaps. We must take advantage of such contradictions as much as possible to create our great advantage. The recapture of Damiao this time was, with the defection of Wang Ying's troops, Shi Yushan and others, as its prelude, which is a clear proof.

Soviet Union Increases Aviation Talent to 150,000

Leningrad. In response to the proposal of workers at the Moscow Manzinsky Aircraft Factory, the Soviet Union will increase its aviation talent to 150,000 in the short term. In order not to hinder the daily work of aviation students, preparations have been made here to expand the number of pilots trained by various aviation clubs. The number of young aviators trained this year has been several times more than in 1935, and it is expected to expand to 14 times the number of last year next year. (TASS dispatch from the 10th)

British Parliament Passes Third Reading: Abdication Bill Becomes Law; Independent Labor Party's Amendment Rejected; New Monarch Set to Ascend the Throne Today, Named "George VI" Instead of "Albert I"

(London) At 1:52 PM today, Parliament announced the King's approval of the Abdication Bill. Edward VIII, who inherited the throne upon the death of George V five minutes before midnight on January 20, 1936, ceased to be the King of England and Emperor of India.

The new British monarch will be Prince Albert, Duke of York, and the Duchess of York will become Queen. Their nine-year-old daughter, Elizabeth, will be the heir apparent.

Both Houses of Parliament passed the Abdication Bill at the third reading within two hours and thirty minutes today, with the solemn rituals of ancient times. Within fifteen minutes, the bill, after receiving royal assent, was announced by the Clerk of Parliament, thus becoming law. Edward VIII has now retired as a commoner and is free to marry his beloved Mrs. Simpson.

This morning, the Prime Minister briefly moved in the Lower House to have the bill read for the second time, reiterating the need to swiftly restore national normalcy and maintain peace. Subsequent speakers echoed this sentiment. Opposition leader Attlee rose to support the bill, stating that the throne was now endangered by vulgar flattery and should be made more ordinary. Liberal Party leader Sinclair also supported the bill. Independent Labor Party member Maxton introduced an amendment to reject the bill and advocate for the abolition of the hereditary throne. Home Secretary Simon followed, stating that recent events have demonstrated how deeply ingrained the concept of constitutional monarchy is in the hearts of the British people. The Lower House then rejected Maxton's amendment by a vote of 403 to 5 and passed the second reading of the bill.

The bill is brief, beginning with a preamble followed by three clauses. The abdication decree is also included in the bill. The first clause is historical and without precedent, stipulating that upon royal assent, the abdication decree shall immediately take effect. Edward VIII will no longer be the monarch, and the crown shall be passed down, therefore to be accepted by whoever in the royal family resolves to inherit the abdication. The second clause stipulates that Edward VIII, his children, and their descendants shall have no rights to the succession to the throne after the abdication. The third clause stipulates that the Royal Marriages Act, which requires royal approval for marriages within the royal family, shall not apply to Edward VIII, his children, and their descendants after the abdication.

During the passage of the bill, Lord Chancellor Somervell responded to questions, stating that the title of Edward VIII should be determined by the new monarch at the appropriate time. The Lord Chancellor also responded to a question from Labor MP Thorne, stating that the claim that Edward VIII would be forced to leave the country was inaccurate. The Lower House then passed the third reading of the bill and sent it to the Upper House, which passed all three readings within fifteen minutes of receiving it from the Lower House. During the passage of the bill in the Lower House, the Lord Chancellor also declared that the revenues enjoyed by the King from England and the Duchies of Cornwall and Lancaster would henceforth belong to the new monarch. What action the Lower House will take in the future is not within the scope of today's discussion. The Prime Minister was the last to speak, saying, "We will never forget all the services of Edward VIII." (Reuters, 11th)

(London) The new monarch, who ascended the throne this afternoon, will be formally proclaimed at St. James's Palace tomorrow afternoon at 3:00 PM. The coronation ceremony is expected to take place around May 5th. The Ministry of Works is continuing its preparations for the coronation ceremony as planned and has not suspended them. (Reuters, 11th)

(London) Monday is the 41st birthday of the new monarch Albert. Various departments of the Empire are preparing to announce the new monarch's accession and celebrate his birthday on that day. The Governor-General of Northern Ireland, the Duke of Abercorn, is convening the Northern Ireland Parliament to meet next week or on Wednesday, at which time the new monarch's succession will be announced. The new monarch's proclamation will then be publicly read in Belfast, Londonderry, and other key areas. Meanwhile, the Australian Federal Parliament has unanimously passed a resolution recognizing the Duke of York's succession to the throne. The governments of Victoria and South Australia have also announced a holiday on Monday, the new monarch's birthday. The New South Wales government has also declared a holiday on Monday and will announce the new monarch's accession on that day. (Reuters, 11th)

Straightforward Advice: Baldwin Did Not Fail as Prime Minister; The Royal Family is the Golden Chain of the British Empire; If Respect for the Monarchy Disappears, Harm Will Follow; Parliament Praises the Abdicating King's Decisiveness

(London) The House of Commons met yesterday afternoon, first with the Speaker reading the Abdication Instrument, followed by Prime Minister Baldwin moving that the Instrument be submitted for discussion. He stated, "The Instrument received by Parliament has never been so serious in nature as this time, and the Prime Minister's responsibilities have never been so difficult as this time." The Prime Minister then recounted the events, saying that he had been friends with Edward VIII before he ascended the throne, and their personal friendship had deepened in recent days of discussion. "In October of this year, various American newspapers had already published various rumors about Mrs. Simpson. People across the Empire were extremely uneasy and sent letters to me inquiring about the truth. Therefore, I thought it was imperative that someone advise the King that allowing such slander to grow would inevitably lead to a serious situation." "However, because it concerned the King himself, only the Prime Minister was responsible for advising him. Therefore, I did not seek the opinions of the cabinet but instead sought the King's approval to meet with him face-to-face without attendants at Fort Belvedere on Tuesday, October 20th, to offer straightforward advice. The King was magnanimous and did not consider it disrespectful. I told the King that although our monarchy has lost some privileges for a long time, its position is far more noble than in the past (applause from the members). Our monarchical system must be kept intact. This is not only the final link connecting the various territories of the British Empire, but also a barrier to prevent the disasters that have occurred in other countries from happening in our country. Furthermore, the people's respect for the royal family has increased over three reigns. If public opinion is allowed to run rampant without restraint, respect for the monarchy will quickly disappear, and it will be very difficult to restore it. For these reasons, I advised the King that it would be very worrying if Mrs. Simpson's divorce proceedings were to continue, and if Mrs. Simpson were to marry the King, she would inevitably be crowned Queen, which the country would never agree to. However, the King told me, 'I am determined to marry Mrs. Simpson and am prepared to abdicate.' Since then, the King consulted with Queen Mary and his brothers, and on November 25th, he summoned me to discuss the plan for a morganatic marriage (referring to marrying Mrs. Simpson without making her Queen). I stated that Parliament would likely not approve of this plan. Subsequently, after I sought the opinions of the cabinet ministers and the prime ministers of the various dominions, they were also unable to agree. I then met with the King again on the 2nd of this month to tell him that this matter was difficult to carry out. ... The King, with a magnanimous spirit, immediately expressed that only by abdicating could he reduce the disputes among the cabinet and the people. If his brother could inherit the throne without difficulty after his abdication, he would be deeply gratified. For this reason, I dare say that anyone who organizes a so-called 'King's Party' in the name of supporting the King is detested by the King (applause from the members). To avoid various demonstrations, the King decided to reside at Fort Belvedere and not leave. He is very close to his brother, the Duke of York, and believes that the subjects of the Empire will unanimously support the Duke after he ascends the throne (applause from the members). ... The King also told me that he could not bear the burden of handling all affairs without a woman's help. However, until the last few days, I was still helping the King find a solution, but to no avail. The King then made his final decision. The government only received the King's reply when it held a cabinet meeting yesterday morning. The cabinet immediately drafted a memorial requesting the King to change his mind, but the King replied that he still believed he could not comply. Although we deeply regret this, we have no other choice but to quickly comply with the King's wishes. Now we must unite and follow the new King to assist him so that the suffering caused by this incident can be quickly healed. We have a heavy responsibility, and we must be loyal from now on so that the country's fortunes will become more prosperous and the people will be blessed." After the Prime Minister finished speaking, the majority of the members of the Lower House applauded and cheered, expressing their approval. Opposition Labor Party leader Attlee suggested adjourning the meeting until 6:00 PM in the afternoon, which was accepted by the Speaker. (Havas, 11th)

The Lower House continued its meeting at 6:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Members of all parties expressed warm praise for the King. Speakers included Labor Opposition Leader Attlee, Liberal Party Leader Sinclair, Conservative Churchill, Independent Labor Party Maxton, and Labor Wedgwood, among others. The Prime Minister then introduced a motion to give effect to the King's abdication declaration. The motion is scheduled to be read for the second time this morning and passed into law before the adjournment of both Houses today. The King's final action was to approve the motion, which meant that the King and his descendants could no longer inherit the throne.

Opposition Leader Attlee immediately rose amid cheers, saying that after reading the lengthy abdication declaration, he could not help but feel sorrow. The whole country will also be deeply saddened by this news. The King's subjects feel that this is their own loss. No one knows the British monarch more deeply than Edward, the King of England, and all subjects of the Empire. We know that the King's heart must be filled with sorrow (cheers from the crowd). The people wanted to find a way to resolve this issue, but all methods were difficult to implement, and they still hoped that it would not lead to abdication. But the King decisively decided to abdicate, and we have no choice but to accept it. Now all the people wish the King a long and happy life in the future. The country has suffered a major shock, and it will take time to recover. It is difficult for anyone to inherit the throne today. We must do our best to lighten his burden. Attlee then offered comfort to Prime Minister Baldwin and, on behalf of the Labor Party, expressed his deepest condolences to the Queen Mother.

Sir Sinclair rose to speak, saying that Edward had faithfully served the country for nearly 25 years, forging a close link between the King and all classes, religions, and races of the Empire. Now that this link has been broken, we feel deeply saddened, especially the King's cabinet members and advisors, most of all the Prime Minister. The Liberal Party congratulates the government on its wisdom in not attempting to divide the country over this issue. The fact that the crown has not fallen into our political debate is due to the King's wisdom. Sinclair also expressed his support for the government's rejection of the morganatic marriage proposal. Sinclair concluded that the one who deserves the greatest sympathy today is the King's beloved brother, the new King, the Duke of York, who has a distinguished record over the years (cheers from the crowd) and a natural inclination towards democracy.

Churchill said, "Mutual recriminations are over and done with. What has not been done should be left to history. I will listen and not ask." No one has ever been able to abide by the letter and spirit of the constitution as well as the current King, because the King has resolutely sacrificed his position for the sake of the country's peace and strength. Churchill continued, "During the turmoil, I advocated for a calm discussion, because if there was any hope that time could bring a solution, we should endure the pain." As far as the government is concerned, the King's decision was not made hastily. Churchill continued, "I accept the Prime Minister's declaration and believe that Edward's final decision was completely voluntary and was not subject to any pressure from others." Churchill also praised Edward's various noble qualities and said that although the country's hope that the King would not abdicate has disappeared, the King's noble character will be immortal, and the poor people of the country will never forget the King. We must now seek to consolidate the throne and give the new King who is succeeding the strength that comes from loving the unity of the Empire. (Reuters, 11th)

Finally, Independent Labor Party member Maxton, Opposition Labor Party member Wedgwood, Communist Party member Gallacher, and Independent Labor Party member Buchanan spoke in succession. Their remarks were radical and unexpected, causing an uproar in the audience. Maxton said, "Past events have proven that the monarchical system is no longer suitable for the times, and the United Kingdom should be changed to a republic." Wedgwood criticized the government, saying that it should not have forced the King to abdicate, because the King was surrounded by villains who used the King's emotions to oppose the cabinet and the constitution. It was impossible for the King to be comfortable in his position. The Labor Party's attitude can be said to have fallen into the government's trap. The labor movement should now express itself in order to extricate itself. Buchanan said, "Those who praise the King are all hypocrites, and their motives are beyond questioning." Finally, Conservative Party member Flannery expressed the veterans' farewell to His Majesty Edward VIII. The Speaker then announced that the first reading of the Abdication Bill was completed and adjourned the meeting until tomorrow. (Havas, 11th)

Members of the Lower House will meet tomorrow to officially swear allegiance to the new monarch. This ceremony will continue next Monday. Parliament has scheduled to begin the Christmas holiday on the 18th of this month. (Reuters, 11th)

Edward Demoted to Commoner, Possesses Little Property

(London) On the day of the death of the late King George V, he gave four million pounds in cash to various grandchildren. The abdicated King Edward VIII was not eligible to share in this inheritance. Therefore, the property owned by the abdicated King is only Fort Belvedere and the savings he had during his time as Duke of Cornwall. Now that he has been demoted to a commoner and calls himself Mr. Windsor, he has no other property to inherit. Therefore, it is generally believed that after the new monarch ascends the throne, he will grant him the title of Duke and the attached property. (Havas, 11th)

Edward Announces Abdication, Dominions Unanimously Regret, Consider it a Tragic Scene in British History, Will Vow Eternal Loyalty to Motherland, South Ireland Prepares to Abolish Governor-General System

Crowds Gather in Front of New Monarch's Residence, Enthusiastic Cheers Shake the Sky

The largest number was in front of the new monarch's residence in Piccadilly. The crowds waited for him to return from Windsor Palace. Preparations for Abdicated King's Departure, Destination Remains Top Secret, Bids Farewell to Friends and Family, Appears Sad and Dejected

The King took this opportunity to bid farewell to his loyal confidants with whom he had spent many years, and walked around the entire building for a final inspection. Mr. Churchill arrived at Fort Belvedere at 1:00 PM this afternoon to have lunch with the King and the Duke of Kent. (Reuters, 11th)

(London) Abdicated King Edward VIII flew out of Hendon Airfield in the suburbs in his own plane, destination unknown. (Havas, 11th)

(London) When Parliament read Edward VIII's abdication instrument today, the King sat alone at Fort Belvedere, stroking his moustache and lost in thought. In the afternoon, the Dukes of York and Gloucester came to visit, and left soon after. Half an hour later, Prime Minister Baldwin presented the abdication instrument in the Lower House. All three of the King's brothers were present when the King signed the instrument. After the abdication, if Parliament allows him to retain the title of Duke of Cornwall, he will still have an annual income of £100,000. The King will probably never set foot on the country again after leaving England, and will never see Queen Mary again. However, the Duke of Kent may meet with him from time to time to maintain family relations. As for where Edward will go first, it is still unknown today. If the final decree of Mrs. Simpson's divorce can take effect earlier, then it may not be necessary to wait until after April 27 next year to get married. Regarding the title after that, it has not been decided today. Court officials said that Edward may give up all his current titles and receive another dukedom. In any case, the government has already prepared for his financial problems. Some observers believe that the King will leave the country as soon as Parliament passes the abdication law and he signs it himself. (National Telegram, 10th)

The Lovers Lead to Honor, Mrs. Simpson is Deeply Moved, Encouraged Via Wireless Telephone

Cannes, France Mrs. Simpson comforted King Edward of England on the wireless telephone today, using rather intimate terms. Mrs. Simpson was greatly impressed that Edward had given up his throne and honor for her. As for Edward's movements, telegrams are sent from time to time to the villa of the American friends Mr. and Mrs. Rogers, where Mrs. Simpson is staying. An Associated Press reporter asked Mr. Rogers if Mrs. Simpson would marry the King. Mr. Rogers replied, "I cannot answer or express an opinion, but judging from the general situation, it seems not far off." Currently, the King and Mrs. Simpson will meet in any day now to avoid legal difficulties that could invalidate the divorce decree due to the meeting. (National Telegram, 10th)

A Short History of the New Emperor

The new Emperor George VI (Albert Frederick Arthur George) is the Duke of York, the second son of the late Emperor George V. Named Albert, he was born on December 14, 1895, just one and a half years younger than his elder brother, Edward. In their youth, he and his brother studied with the same tutors and played together until his brother entered the Worthy Marine Training School. In 1909, he also went to Worthpoint, attending the same school as his brother, at the age of fourteen. After two years, he transferred to Dartmouth to continue his studies. He then boarded an officer training ship to experience the ocean winds and waves. The Emperor loved mechanics and was very skilled in sailing. In his mind, the navy was his future. The Emperor operated on the ship with the other officer cadets, without receiving special treatment as a royal. One day, the late Emperor boarded the ship for inspection. The Emperor took his place in the line as usual. Although father and son had been apart for several months, the Emperor passed before his father without hesitation. On May 31, 1916, in the great Battle of Jutland, the Emperor, as a naval lieutenant, served in the forward turret of the cruiser "Columbus," commanding the twelve-inch caliber guns. He remained calm under intense fire. His courage was admired by all the officers and men on the ship. As a royal son, participating in naval warfare had not happened since another Duke of York fought the Dutch army off the coast of Lowestoft 250 years ago. Later, the ship presented the Emperor with the flag it had flown during the great battle as a souvenir. After the Battle of Jutland, the Emperor suffered from a severe stomach ailment, seemingly ending his beloved naval career. However, he continued to serve on the staff of the Commander-in-Chief of the Portsmouth Naval Base. In July 1919, he obtained a pilot's license, allowing him to serve in the Air Ministry.

After the outbreak of the European War, many young men in the country lost their education due to joining the army. The Emperor was one of them. In the year of the war's end, the Emperor entered Cambridge University to further his studies, focusing on history, economics, and civics. Although the Emperor did not attend every lecture, his exceptional talent allowed him to gain considerable knowledge. The small pieces of paper signed "Prince A" by the Emperor during lectures were often taken from the storage box by souvenir collectors after the lectures, who treasured them as precious objects.

In June 1920, on the late Emperor's birthday, honors were bestowed upon the Emperor, making him the Duke of York, Earl of Inverness, and Baron Killarney. Three years later, in April 1923, he married Miss Elizabeth Bowes-Lyon at Westminster Abbey. At that time, the people rejoiced and contributed £2,500 for a wedding gift, which the Emperor donated to poor children. In the following years, the couple hunted in East Africa, capturing animals such as lions, elephants, and leopards. They also officially toured Australia and various dominions in the Southern Hemisphere. During his visit to Canberra, Australia, he presided over the opening ceremony of the new Parliament House. Everyone who came into contact with the Emperor admired his sincerity and kindness, which greatly increased the people's respect and love for the royal family. In 1928, the late Emperor's health deteriorated, and the Emperor was appointed as one of the six regents. The following year, the two major denominations of Scotland, which had been divided for many years, reunited. The Emperor represented his father at the ceremony in Edinburgh, with the Duchess accompanying him. Witnessing the grand ceremony, the couple said with emotion, "Our children should be brought into society early to broaden their horizons." At that time, the couple often brought their three-year-old daughter, Elizabeth. The following August, another daughter, named Rose, was born. The new Emperor is tall and handsome, with a gentle and solemn appearance, resembling his father more than his brothers. The Emperor is exceptionally kind and loves children. He often plays with his two daughters, tirelessly enjoying himself. At night, unless detained by business, he always goes to his daughters' rooms to say "goodnight." The Emperor is not only a loving father but also a faithful husband, so the couple is very affectionate. Wherever he goes, the Duchess always accompanies him. The new Emperor is very enthusiastic about social affairs. During his tours of various industrial towns, he visited even the poorest neighborhoods, leaving his footprints everywhere, hoping to broaden his knowledge and understand the hardships of the people. He cares about the people's suffering in this way. Once, during an inspection of a rubber factory, his followers told him that one area had a foul odor and he did not need to go there. The Emperor became angry and said, "How can that be? If the people can work there, why can't I go?" The Emperor often said that the two main characteristics of a leader should be idealism and compassion. The Emperor has a deep understanding of these two characteristics. One day, a child in a camp called the Emperor "a human being." The Emperor considered this the highest honor he had ever received.

Because the Emperor loves children and deeply believes that the future of the country depends on the goodwill and cooperation of all sectors of society, he annually gathers four hundred boys aged seventeen to nineteen for camping and recreation. Half of them are selected from public schools such as Eton, and the rest are selected from working children in various industrial centers. The purpose of this is to break down class barriers. Every summer, the boys live together in a camp for two weeks. Their work, sports, and swimming are all equal, and there is no class distinction. All the boys must wear loose shirts and shorts according to the rules. The Emperor also wears this attire and often spends one or two days with them. When he arrives at the camp, the boys cheer, because the Emperor always works with the boys, sometimes swimming. When tired of resting on the beach, he hands out snacks to the children, and they all chew together happily. The Emperor likes playing ball and fishing, and he is skilled in riding and shooting. In his youth, he studied radio diligently. The two radio stations in Buckingham Palace are all supervised and operated by the Emperor. After the birth of his daughters, he personally wired the nursery. The Emperor is good at driving cars. Whenever he goes out, although there is a driver, he likes to drive long distances himself. The Emperor loves hunting very much, but in 1931, due to the country's financial difficulties, the royal family reduced expenses and sold all his hunting dogs. (Reuters, November 11)

Preparations for the Coronation Ceremony: Huge Losses for Merchants, Souvenirs Unable to Be Sold

(London) Merchants who manufacture coronation ceremony souvenirs will suffer significant losses due to Emperor Edward's abdication. It is estimated that there are over eight million pieces of pottery manufactured for the coronation ceremony that are now unable to be sold. Large quantities of cotton and rayon goods bearing portraits of Emperor Edward have been completely discarded. Fortunately, some items only feature national flags and royal crown designs, which can be modified and sold during the new Emperor's coronation. Manufacturers of cheap souvenirs have suffered greatly this time. Tens of thousands of newly printed prayer books are now obsolete. Newly printed stamps by the post office will also be canceled entirely. It is reported that the mint had prepared to issue new coins in the New Year, but the currency of Edward VIII will no longer circulate in the world. (Reuters, November 11)

British Press Commentary

(London) Today, British newspapers unanimously expressed regret over Emperor Edward's abdication. While The Times also expressed this sentiment, its editorial offered rather blunt discussions of Emperor Edward's "stubbornness" and "habit of imprudence in foreign society." The newspaper stated that the throne and the empire had been greatly shaken, but would soon return to normal. "We now have to say that Emperor Edward had too many male and female friends, and most of them grew up in wealthy families. They rarely approached the people, so all their actions only considered their own entertainment and neglected the Emperor's happiness. The real conflict this time lies in the habit of imprudence in foreign society and the unwavering traditional thinking and behavior of Britain. We can see the Emperor's stubbornness in his irrevocable decision this time," it said. The Daily Mail reported that the pain in Emperor Edward's heart when he made the decision to abdicate was not difficult to imagine, but it could be asserted that the people would therefore increase their respect and sympathy for the Emperor. The Daily Telegraph said that the publication of Emperor Edward's abdication decree shocked the world. Because the Emperor usually won the hearts of the people so deeply, the public would not refuse any request he made. However, they were also driven by their duties. For example, the Emperor's request this time was for his beloved marriage for happiness, but in the eyes of the nation, they all believed that it would damage the dignity of the throne and the prestige of the country and had to be rejected. The Morning Post, in addition to expressing regret over Emperor Edward's abdication, also extended unlimited hope to the new monarch. The Glasgow Herald praised Emperor Edward's proper attitude and Prime Minister Baldwin's great statesmanlike demeanor, saying that the result of this issue today was due to the strength of the two men. The Scotsman's opinion was that the announcement of the abdication decree may not be the end of this incident. It must be known that Emperor Edward's future is full of thorns, and he should not be stubborn in his private opinions and disregard the hopes of the whole country. (Reuters, November 11)

League of Nations Council Meeting: Spanish Foreign Minister Cries Out Loudly, Accuses Italy and Germany of Interfering in Spanish Civil War, Hopes League of Nations Will Take Effective Measures to Stop It

(Geneva) The temporary meeting of the League of Nations Council, which opened yesterday, held an open meeting at 11:30 this morning. The Spanish Foreign Minister Álvarez del Vayo delivered a long speech, stating that the Spanish government's appeal to the League of Nations was to prevent the domestic civil war from causing serious international repercussions. The fact that the British and French governments had proposed to Italy, Germany, Portugal, and Russia to stop interfering showed that the Spanish government's actions were fully justified. As for the war in Spain, although various countries had established a non-intervention agreement, hundreds of thousands of lives had died in the trenches, still victims of fascist air forces and foreign military supplies. At this point, Álvarez del Vayo cried out loudly, "A cruel war is underway, and this war is an international war within Spain!" He then said that after the Spanish rebel army suffered losses in Morocco, "foreign soldiers" (referring to volunteers from Italy and Germany) went to help them. The rebel army did not hesitate to use poison gas to kill government troops. If the rebel army were to win in the future, Italy and Germany might try to take possession of the Balearic Islands in the western Mediterranean, or even other naval bases. People often have a concept of peace, thinking that as long as peace can be maintained on the surface, it is okay to compromise. However, while this compromise is taking place, cities are being razed to ruins, and countless thousands are dying. This concept of peace is not to be followed. Álvarez del Vayo then listed the reasons for the Spanish government's appeal, saying that Italy and Germany recognized the Spanish rebel government as the legitimate government. The ports belonging to the government forces on the Spanish coast were in danger of being blockaded. "The power of the League of Nations has failed to prevent acts of aggression. Now, the disaster of a prairie fire is approaching. It is hoped that the League of Nations can at least prevent the spread of the war." Some say that convening a temporary meeting of the Council will lead to the expansion of the war. This statement is not accurate. It is hoped that the Council meeting will achieve concrete results on the Spanish civil war and not just be a preliminary and passive indication. Although Spain still supports the basic principles of the non-intervention agreement signed by various countries, given the different circumstances, it believes that this agreement has failed to take effect, which is already obvious. The urgent task is to remedy the defects of the non-intervention policy and strictly implement monitoring measures. However, the so-called monitoring measures must genuinely be effective, which is what Spain most desires. After Álvarez del Vayo finished his speech, the Council extended the meeting until 5:30 PM. (Havas, November 11)

British Army and Navy Chiefs Announce Wartime Industrial Mobilization Plan: Control of Exports of Major Items

(Washington) Secretary of War Woodring and Secretary of the Navy Swanson separately announced today the outline of the U.S. industrial mobilization plan. Its contents stipulate that once a war occurs, the government will implement control policies for major items such as sugar, coffee, rubber, ordnance, military supplies, and transportation, as well as foreign and territorial trade. Once this mobilization bill is passed by Congress, President Roosevelt will have the power to declare when ordnance, military supplies, and other special goods (67 kinds) can be exported, as well as the quantity of exports. The bill also stipulates the organization of a Wartime Trade Management Committee to promote cooperation among government agencies, specializing in handling passport regulations and setting prices, in order to implement the control of import and export trade and exert economic pressure on enemy countries. (National Telegram, November 10)

A Certain Party's Strategy of Aggression Changes Frequently, Failed to Counterattack Bailingmiao, Is Now Turning to Eastern Sui and Xinghe, Actively Increasing Troops and Transporting Weapons on the Southern Trench Front, A Certain Person Left Doron for Kangbao and Baochang

Zhangbei Communication: The war situation in the Taolin and Xinghe areas of eastern Sui and central Sui has been quite silent recently. The bandits and puppets who counterattacked Bailingmiao have repeatedly failed. Wang Ying, Li Shouxin, and others are at their wits' end. There are even reports that Wang and Li have engaged in infighting, further revealing their state of elimination. The "certain party" behind the scenes, also seeing that our army's defensive lines are tightly guarded and that the bandit and puppet troops have repeatedly collapsed, has lost their sense of underestimating the enemy. The northward and eastward advances have been blocked everywhere. Therefore, their strategies have also changed frequently, sometimes trying to invade northern Sui, sometimes harassing Xinghe and Taolin, without any direction. According to a person from Jiabus in Temple on the 8th, a certain special agency in Jiabus in Temple issued a message that the Japanese Kwantung Army was extremely dissatisfied with the repeated counterattacks by the bandits and puppets. Therefore, it has ordered the leaders of the bandits and puppets not to allow any more defeats in the future. If anyone performs poorly in battle, their superiors will be questioned and severely punished. They will implement the use of the Jehol bandit army as the main force to invade Sui, ordering their regular troops to enter northern Chahar and occupy various places. As for the current strategy, because northern Sui is difficult to obtain, they have decided to invade Xinghe from the Southern Trench in eastern Sui, attempting to obtain Pingdiquan (Jining) to cut off the Ping-Sui Railway traffic and control the passage for Sui province's reinforcements and transportation. As for the puppet troops entrenched in the Southern Trench, they were originally the elite of Li Shouxin's troops, stationed in the Daqinggou area. Now, Li's troops are gradually moving to Shangdu and Jiabus in Temple, and there are very few remaining in the Southern Trench. Although Zhang Wanqing's brigade of Wang Ying's bandit troops in the Southern Trench is called two brigades, it actually has only about two thousand men. In addition, the rest are all Jehol bandits, Zhang Junzhe and Li Zhenming, who are constantly being supplemented. There are also many regular troops of a "certain party" mixed in. The total is more than six thousand people. Now, another three thousand Jehol bandits are concentrating in Shimulu in the Zhangbei County area and will go to the Southern Trench within days. According to the bandits and puppets, after ten thousand people have gathered in the Southern Trench, they will launch a fierce attack on Xinghe. On the evening of the 7th, more than a dozen commanders of a "certain party" arrived in Zhangbei from Jiabus in Temple. On the 8th, they went to the Southern Trench by car to take charge of commanding operations. It is expected that a fierce battle will break out there soon.

The "certain party" has driven all the bandits and puppets to the front line, and is using its regular troops and the Jehol puppet army to occupy northern Chahar, which was its original plan. Now that the two puppet forces of Wang Ying and Li Shouxin are almost eliminated, and the Mongolian puppet army is also taking care of itself, it is an excellent opportunity to implement its plan. Now, in addition to the Kawakishi Brigade stationed in northern Chahar, its regular troops and the Jehol puppet army have gradually moved into northern Chahar from Jehol recently. On the evening of the 7th, more than five thousand regular troops of a "certain party" and the Jehol puppet army, who had already arrived in Doron, headed west from Doron, and went to Kangbao, Tianchang, and Yulingou and Gaoshanpu in Guyuan County, to occupy key locations in northern Chahar. The rest of the troops are currently preparing to move west from Jehol. Since the "certain party" launched the Sui border war, a large number of military supplies have been transported from the Northeast or Tianjin to Zhangbei, constantly supplying the bandits and puppets. On the 1st of this month, they distributed more than 700,000 yuan in military pay to the bandits and puppets at the Jiabus Temple checkpoint. It is now heard that the "certain party" has another large batch of military supplies, transported from Tianjin to Zhangjiakou on the 6th, with a total of six train cars and 180 tons, which will be transported here by car and then distributed to the bandits and puppets in batches. Since the 6th, a large number of military supplies and needs have been transported from Zhangbei to the Southern Trench in the past few days. On the 8th, more than a dozen trucks of sacks were transported. It is said that after these sacks arrived in the Southern Trench that day, they were received by the traitor Zhang Wanqing. Zhang then ordered dozens of local laborers to fill each sack with yellow earth and then pile them outside the positions and trenches for cover. (8th)

National Government Financial Advisor, Newson, Assassinated by Bandits in Henan; Newson Was the Manager of Xuchang Tobacco Company; An Employee of Xuchang Company Also Killed

Zhengzhou Correspondence: Wu Tingsheng, manager of Xuchang Tobacco Company, was assassinated in Xuchang last winter, but the perpetrator remained at large. Wu’s son, Wu Shenxiong, accused Nie Wanqing and Yu Shijun in the Xuchang court of being the murderers of Wu. The court, finding the evidence insufficient, dismissed the case by the prosecutor. Wu Shenxiong then applied to the Henan High Court for reconsideration. The High Court transferred the case to the Zhengzhou District Court for jurisdiction and trial. After accepting the case, the court held several trials. Unexpectedly, before the verdict was announced, a witness (Wu Tingsheng's attendant) suddenly disappeared in Zhengzhou. The Zhengzhou court again declared the defendants Nie Wanqing, Yu Shijun, etc., not guilty due to insufficient evidence. It is said that the prosecutor of the Zhengzhou court will appeal this case. Unexpectedly, the Wu case has not yet been concluded, and the manager of Xuchang Tobacco Company, the American Newson, (a native of Salisbury, North Carolina, USA, currently 40 years old, whose wife and young daughter reside in Hankou, and his elderly mother still resides in his hometown, Newson currently serves as a financial advisor to the National Government) was robbed of his property and shot dead by bandits in his office at 6 p.m. on the 4th of this month. In addition, Guo Shuxian, an employee of the company, was injured and died one hour before Newson. A policeman outside the window of the office was also injured in the head by a bandit bullet. Fortunately, the injury was relatively minor, and if no other morbid conditions occur recently, his life can be saved without worry. After hearing the news, the reporter immediately went to Xuchang from Zhengzhou on the morning of the 5th to investigate and returned to Zhengzhou that evening. The details of the Newson case are recorded as follows:

According to Bi Zhiyun, director of the Xuchang Tobacco Company's tobacco factory, the situation of bandits rushing into the office to rob and shoot Newson and Guo Shuxian is as follows: The office of our company consists of eight interconnected rooms in two sections, four rooms on the east and four on the west, with a side passage in the middle. Newson's office is in the first room on the east side, and the lending room is in the fourth room on the west side. At about 6 p.m. that evening, while the lending office was distributing funds to tobacco farmers, a group of bandits suddenly rushed into the office. One bandit stood at the entrance of the office. There were two bandits entering the lending room, one guarding the outside and one inside. In the passageway of the office, there was an attendant sweeping the floor. Suddenly seeing the bandits, he immediately asked what they were doing. The bandits told him not to make a sound and went forward to take away his broom. The attendant, in a moment of urgency and resourcefulness, immediately ran out and shouted "Bandits! Bandits!" Newson, hearing the alarm, rushed into the lending room from his office with a handgun. At that time, Guo Shuxian, an employee in the lending room, was negotiating a loan with Zhou Jintang, manager of the Longhe Company. Suddenly hearing someone behind him, he turned around and saw a bandit standing there with a gun, telling him not to make a sound, and that they were only there for some money. Guo Shuxian immediately replied, "Please take whatever you want." The bandit then robbed the money being distributed on the table. At this time, Newson entered the room with a gun, pointing the muzzle at the bandit and asking what he was doing. The bandit, seeing the situation was not good, shouted loudly in the room, "Why not shoot?" (According to the bandit, "shoot" meant ordering the bandit standing outside the room to shoot Newson). The bandit standing outside the lending room heard the words and immediately shot Newson with a gun. The bullet entered from his right back and exited from his left chest, and he fell to the ground immediately. The bandit standing opposite Newson was also knocked down by him. The bandit quickly got up and shot Guo Shuxian in the room, the bullet hitting his forehead above the center of his eyebrows. The bullet did not exit, and Guo also fell to the ground in response. When the attendant, who was sweeping the floor in the passageway, ran out and shouted "Bandits!", the bandit guarding the door fired three shots at him, but missed. Another employee, Guan Jing, came out from the office opposite the lending room, and the bandit standing opposite Newson fired a shot at him. Unexpectedly, the gun misfired, and he was fortunate not to be injured. Seeing that the robbery was not going well, this bandit immediately returned to the lending room, snatched the gun held by Newson, and shouted, "Hurry, let's go!" At this time, a policeman was standing guard outside the window of the lending room. Seeing the bandit alarm, he looked for a hiding place, preparing to shoot the bandits. Unexpectedly, he was attacked from behind by another bandit with a shot, the bullet passing through the skin and breaking the bone on the upper right side of his head. He immediately fainted on the ground. According to the policeman, when he was injured and fainted, he was still mentally conscious and heard the bandits shout "Hurry, let's go!" and then they escaped out of the north gate of the courtyard. According to the doctors at the Xuchang American Hospital, after Newson and others were injured and carried into the hospital, Newson's bullet wound penetrated the heart through the spinal bone, entering from the back and exiting from the front chest. The specific vertebrae of the spine that were injured were not examined in detail. While he was being treated in the hospital, we told him that Newson's injuries were serious, but he was confident that his life was not in danger, saying, "It's okay, it's okay." But the fact that most of the blood from the gunshot wound did not flow out indicates that the fresh blood has entered the internal organs, and his life is in danger. Newson died of his injuries at 10:30 p.m. that evening. Guo Shuxian, who was killed at the same time as Newson, had a bullet shot into his head from the front upper forehead towards the back. The bullet did not exit. Because it hit a vital point, he lost too much blood and died an hour before Newson. Regarding the aftermath of Newson and Guo, the company has prepared a coffin to encoffinate Newson and transport him to Hankou on the 5th. Guo's coffin will be prepared and buried by Zhou Jintang, manager of the Longhe Company. The Fifth District Administrative Commissioner's Office is paying close attention to this case because Xuchang is the location of the Commissioner's Office, and bandits dared to rob with guns and injure people. It has ordered the arrest of the murderers and a thorough investigation.

Drought and Food Shortage in Sichuan and Henan Provinces; Purchasing Large Quantities of Rice from Anhui Province; Wuhu Rice Market Becomes Active; Tianjin and Military Needs Also Compete to Purchase in Wuhu

Wuhu Correspondence: This year, Henan Province has had little rainfall, resulting in a severe drought. The affected counties are estimated to be more than 70. The autumn harvest has already failed, and wheat has not been planted. Grain prices have soared, and the people lack food. The provincial Pingtiao Bureau, in charge of price stabilization, should purchase various grains from neighboring provinces with abundant harvests to regulate the market and alleviate the disaster. Since Anhui Province has sufficient grain and low prices, a letter was sent to the Wuhu Chamber of Commerce, instructing local grain merchants to quickly fill out a price list of various grains and send it as soon as possible for procurement. It was also requested that a list be sent every ten days thereafter for reference. Sichuan Province, also suffering from severe disasters and high grain prices, has sent personnel to Wuhu to purchase relief rice and transport it back to provide assistance. As a result, the rice market here has suddenly become active. In addition to Sichuan's relief rice and Tianjin's tobacco merchants competing for purchases, military demand is also very strong. The daily average transaction at the dock is 17,000 to 18,000 bags. Prices on the 10th were two dimes higher than on the 8th and 9th. Based on this, there is still a tendency for prices to continue to rise. Currently, the market price of September red glutinous rice is 10.34 to 10.56 yuan per stone, Zihuo 9.78 yuan, Nanling machine-milled Xian rice 9.34 yuan, brown rice 8.16 to 7.78 yuan, and Chao County and Yellow River sluice machine-milled rice both open at 9.23 yuan. Lujiang Ma Xian 9.34 yuan, machine-milled rice 8.78 to 9 yuan. As for yellow soybeans among miscellaneous grains, due to the recent increased demand from Yantai and other areas, people are scrambling to buy them, so sales are expanding. However, due to the scarcity of sources and insufficient inventory, prices have risen by more than one dime. On the 10th, 700 to 800 bags were traded at the dock, with Jiangbei yellow soybeans opening at 7.7 yuan, Zhongguang 7.45 yuan, and Zihuo 7.12 yuan (10th).

Completion of Nine-Province Telephone Network; Wuhu-Hangzhou Calls Start on the 10th; Anhui Provincial Telephone Network Also Nears Completion

Wuhu Correspondence: The long-distance telephone lines of the nine provinces have been gradually completed in sections. Wuhu has already been connected to major ports such as Beijing, Shanghai, Hankou, and Jiujiang, with clear sound, making it feel like being in the same room thousands of miles away. It is learned that the long-distance telephone lines between Wuhu and Hangzhou, Wuxing in Zhejiang, and Guanyun in Jiangsu will also start operation on the 10th. The fee from Wuhu to Hangzhou is one yuan per call, to Wuxing nine dimes, and to Guanyun one yuan and six dimes. As for the long-distance telephone lines between counties independently constructed by Anhui Province, more than 40 places have recently been completed. The counties in the second administrative district of Wuhu, and important counties such as Wuhu, Fanchang, Dangtu, and Xuancheng, have gradually been connected. The Wunan Line (Nanling County) telephone is also currently being installed. The Wuhu poles have been erected to the Sanbu tube. Once the engineering in Nanling County is completed, calls will also begin. However, due to the separation of Wuhu and Wuwei by the Yangtze River, the installation of underwater lines is a huge project. Although preparations are underway, it is feared that completion will be difficult in the short term (10th).

Amidst Support for Suiyuan, Guangdong's Public Sentiment is Indignant and Agitated; Strict Prevention of People with Hidden Nationalities Mixing in Urban Areas; Patriots Organize Iron-Blood National Salvation Corps

Guangzhou Correspondence: Amidst the urgent diplomatic situation, foreigners often mix in the markets in Guangzhou, or create incidents, hoping to cause trouble, or use leased shops to engage in smuggling. For example, recently at a certain hotel in Xidi, a foreigner and the person sitting next to him quarreled over a small matter, roaring and causing trouble in the shop. Afterwards, after the police mediated in many ways, they escorted the person back to the Shamian Concession, and the matter subsided. Not long after, cases of people of certain nationalities fraudulently leasing shops and disputes arising in Fengning Road and other places in the city occurred. The citizens are now automatically taking strict precautions. For any shops for rent, the rental declaration must state that the lessee must find a shop to guarantee that they are not a foreigner before renting. The police authorities also ordered each branch bureau to register any shops for rent in their jurisdiction. The landlord must not lease to foreigners without authorization. In addition, they ordered the patrolling police to pay attention to household registration movements. For long-term residents, they must pay attention to the landlord's actions and memorize the names of the householders and guests to prevent spies from mixing in. Recently, some people in the city have organized the Iron-Blood National Salvation Corps with the purpose of eliminating traitors, engaging in open activities in the city and sending people to distribute leaflets, explaining the definition of traitors as follows: (1) Using language, writing, or other methods to publicize the strength of the enemy, thereby anesthetizing and intimidating the Chinese people, so that consciously or unconsciously, they willingly submit to the enemy; (2) Reporting China's national defense equipment and plans, and plans and methods to prevent enemy invasion of China to the enemy; (3) Running errands and lobbying for the enemy or guiding the enemy to spy on various situations in China, in order to help the enemy invade China; (4) Colluding with the enemy to engage in smuggling and tax evasion; (5) Leasing or buying houses and land for the enemy; (6) Leasing or selling houses and land to the enemy with prior knowledge; (7) Colluding with the enemy with the intention of disrupting China's peace and order; (8) Harboring or hiding the enemy to plot wrongdoing, endangering China's public security; (9) Selling red pills, heroin, or other drugs to the enemy to harm the health of Chinese citizens; (10) Other acts willingly engaged in that benefit the enemy and harm China's national system, sovereignty, national interests, and social security. The above ten principles are the targets of the group's activities. It is said that if they are discovered in the city, they will be eliminated without hesitation or leniency and advise citizens not to intentionally or unintentionally act as accomplices for the enemy, cutting themselves off from their homes and country (December 6).

Jiading: All Sectors Vigorously Support Suiyuan

Since the county education association and others initiated the Suiyuan support movement in the county, the county junior high school has already donated more than 200 yuan, the county vocational school has donated more than 90 yuan, and seven private ordinary schools have donated a total of more than 100 yuan. The rural teachers from Kunshan, Jiading and Qingpu counties are donating their money that they saved from eating porridge.
