Recent Conditions in Wusong City: Business Sluggish, Not Recovered to Pre-War State; Pig Industry's Move to Shanghai May Affect Wusong

Since the January 28th Incident, Wusong, with its wide and orderly streets and novel and beautiful buildings, does appear more aesthetically pleasing and magnificent upon superficial observation than before. However, the market's desolation and the sluggishness of business have not recovered to their pre-war state. The reason for this is that Wusong is located at the mouth of the sea, and in the past, cargo ships shuttled in and out like weaving, making it a hub for shipping merchants, hence the old name "Water Wharf." Since the National Government implemented the system of cutting transit duties and increasing taxes, tax collection agencies such as customs and tax bureaus have all been abolished. Merchants passing through no longer need to stop. In addition, the relocation of army, navy, and police forces to other locations has caused the market to plummet. Currently, what sustains it are the emerging pig industry in the east town, the Wing On and Hua Feng spinning mills, and the Zhanghuabang Railway General Machinery Factory in the west town. Therefore, various businesses can still manage to maintain operations. However, recently there have been two events that could significantly affect the prosperity and decline of Wusong City. The first is the relocation of the Railway General Machinery Factory. The factory has received an order from the Railway Bureau, for the sake of facilitating railway engineering, to move the entire factory to near Qishuyan outside the South Gate of Changzhou. They have already begun to gradually relocate, and it is said that the relocation will be completed within one or two years. Once the relocation is completed, all departments of the factory, including staff, artisans, railway police, laborers, and servants, along with their families, will inevitably leave with the factory. This will reduce the population of Wusong City. The second is the proposed relocation of the pig industry back to South Shanghai. The Shanghai and Wusong factions are secretly brewing this intensely. Since the January 28th Incident, the municipal government stipulated that Yizhoutang in Wusong should be the area for fresh pig stockades. Shanghai pig businesses have flocked to Wusong to set up branches, and pig sties have been built with basic facilities. Therefore, in the past two years, in addition to the original three pig businesses, the number has expanded to about twenty. The staff, stockade managers, lightermen, carters, and pig merchants of each business have added more than several hundred households to the residents of Wusong. Recently, Shanghai businesses, considering the inconvenience of doing business and the enormous expenses, have jointly submitted a petition to the municipal government, requesting permission to relocate back to the vicinity of Gaochang Temple in South Shanghai for business, calling it "centralization," which has aroused opposition from Wusong businesses. However, Wusong only has four businesses: Wan Shen, Jia Tai, Yuan Tai, Hong Da, etc., and their strength is far inferior to that of Shanghai businesses. However, Wusong businesses have a formal reason for opposition, saying that the stipulation of the pig sty area was based on the order of the municipal government and has not been implemented for long. However, the pig industry's business is all within the scope of the urban area, and they should comply with the municipal government's order. Therefore, the weighing of this matter rests with the municipal government. Whether it can revoke the previous order remains to be seen.

Labor Service Propaganda Held in Gaoqiao Yesterday

At 1:00 PM yesterday, the city's Labor Service Committee convened a discussion meeting in Rixin Elementary School, Gaoqiao Town, to discuss matters related to labor service propaganda in the area. Yu Zhenhui, a representative of the Labor Service Committee, was then asked to instruct on the propaganda guidelines, and then the discussion began, and the following propaganda methods were decided: (1) Propaganda week will be held starting next week; (2) Make use of the opportunity to investigate school-age children to publicize as much as possible; (3) Compile propaganda phrases and have storytellers in teahouses publicize them; (4) Regularly hold costume speeches, with the Rural Improvement Association, the Security Corps, the Public Security Bureau, the District Farmers' Association, and all public and private schools in the district responsible for organizing them. Taiping Mountain Outside Wusong Establishes Calcium Carbide Lamp; Privately Installed Lights Have Been Taken Over; Because It Is a Key Navigation Route for Numerous Sailing Vessels

Taiping Mountain, belonging to Zhejiang province outside Wusong, is also one of the Zhoushan Islands. Fishing boats and other sailing vessels travel to and fro throughout the year, forming a continuous stream. Therefore, the residents of the island raised funds to privately install a fixed oil lamp to facilitate ship navigation. The Jianghai Customs, recognizing that the light is crucial for navigation, has officially taken over the lamp and installed a new white tower (280 feet above high tide) with an unattended calcium carbide flashing light. The light has a range of 10 nautical miles and was lit on the 18th of this month. The lamp is located at 121 degrees 19 minutes 9 seconds east longitude and 30 degrees 5 minutes north latitude, near the northwest corner of Taiping Mountain.

Kuaili Breaks Anchor Chain

The Kuaili, a state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company vessel, originally sailed the middle reaches of the Yangtze River from Hankou to Shashi and Yichang. Recently, due to the shallowing of the Yangtze River (yesterday, the draft limit between Hankou and Xunyang was 10 feet), making it difficult for large ships to navigate, the Kuaili was telegraphed to Shanghai to operate a direct service to Yisha. On this voyage, when the ship arrived near Liuhaisha's Pitmankin Light Vessel at night, three large junks suddenly appeared, without lights, attempting to cross the bow of the Kuaili. At the time, the northwest wind was very strong, and they were approaching aggressively. The Kuaili was fully loaded with cargo and passengers. If it continued forward, it would inevitably collide, causing a major accident. If it tried to avoid the collision by veering to the side, it would run aground in the shallow sand. Captain Gu Shurong quickly reversed the engines and dropped both anchors to avoid the collision. The three junks safely passed, and the Kuaili was fortunate not to run aground. However, when the two anchors were dropped, one anchor lost its balance due to a short chain (four sections), and the anchor chain snapped. One large iron anchor sank to the bottom of the river. After inspection, it was found that 5,948 feet of anchor chain was lost, and the anchor that sank weighed 2,240 pounds, totaling a loss of several thousand yuan. Now that the ship has arrived in Shanghai, the head office has been notified, and a new chain and anchor must be installed.

Two Workers Seriously Injured in Truck Fall

Yun Chang Coal Depot at No. 21 Fengji Wharf Street in Nanshi specializes in coal for tiger stoves, so business is booming. It has two trucks for transporting goods, and every morning it loads fuel and distributes it to various users. At around 7:00 AM yesterday, the No. 2 truck, loaded with coal, was traveling on Lujiabang Road when, due to excessive speed, the large sacks of coal piled on the truck suddenly collapsed, and two laborers standing on the truck fell at the same time, both suffering serious injuries. The police arrived and impounded the vehicle that caused the accident. They immediately called an ambulance to take the two injured laborers to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. One, Zhang Zhiming, 25 years old, from Suqian, suffered a fractured skull and brain injury. He died shortly after due to excessive bleeding. The other, Jia Zhenfei, 27 years old, from Suqian, suffered injuries to his head, face, waist, and other parts of his body and was unconscious. It is said that his life is also in critical condition.

Concession Tax Collectors Should Pay Attention to Regulations

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "We respectfully inform you that, according to a letter from the Dazhonglou Restaurant, a taxpayer, 'Our restaurant, located at No. 706 at the intersection of Edward Road and Yunnan Road, has been in business for ten years. The quarterly liquor tax has always been 21 yuan, and the food tax has been 10 yuan. This winter, the food tax was suddenly changed to 30 yuan, an increase of 20 yuan per quarter compared to before. When we inquired about the reason for the increase, the tax collector refused to explain. Subsequently, every time they came to collect, they were accompanied by police officers, and their language was often coercive. Paying taxes is the duty of citizens. Even if the economy is extremely difficult, we try our best to raise the money and have never asked for a slight reduction. Now, the tax is suddenly increased several times. What is the reason? It is incomprehensible. If it is based on seating capacity, all three floors were used for our own use when the restaurant was first established. After 1930, we began to rent out the ground floor due to sluggish business. To this day, the ground floor has not been reclaimed, and the seating capacity on the second and third floors remains the same as in 1930 and has not been increased or expanded. If it is based on the state of the market, the business situation is even worse compared to 1930, and there is no need for our restaurant to provide evidence. We believe that your department has felt the pain of the worsening situation over the years. However, at this time of economic difficulties, it is truly perplexing to suddenly double the tax. We have reported the details of what happened and request that you forward this to the department and cancel the extra ten yuan of food tax per quarter. After all, the economic policy of killing the goose that lays the golden eggs is not a way to develop financial resources. Your association is the voice of taxpayers. Please advocate for fairness.' Upon receiving the letter, we found that there are specific regulations for the collection of various taxes, which taxpayers use as a basis, and tax collectors should follow. However, your department's tax collectors not only do not collect taxes according to the tax regulations, but they also increase or decrease taxes at will. Although there are specific regulations, they are equivalent to waste paper. Such actions are bound to cause trouble, causing taxpayers to dispute frequently over tax payments. According to the above, we request that your department promptly instruct the relevant department to strictly warn the tax collectors to pay attention to the tax regulations, understand the social economy, and not cause disturbances, so as to ensure commercial stability."

After the Death of Gu Rongfen, a British Missionary Stationed in Guizhou, the Guizhou Branch of the China International Famine Relief Commission Will Erect a Monument in His Memory for His Contributions

Mr. Gu Rongfen, a British national, had been teaching in Guizhou for more than 40 years and was very enthusiastic about charitable work. In 1920, the Guizhou Branch of the China International Famine Relief Commission was established, and he was appointed as an honorary treasurer. Mr. Gu readily accepted the position and was very responsible for the safekeeping of funds. When Tang Jiyao was in charge of Guizhou, the Commission remitted 160,000 yuan to Guizhou, which was demanded by the guest army. Mr. Gu negotiated back and forth, exhausting himself, and finally managed to have the entire amount returned to avoid embezzlement. The Guizhou Branch has been able to maintain its operations until today, thanks to this money. Mr. Gu passed away due to illness a month ago, at the age of 68. The Branch, in recognition of his contributions to famine relief in Guizhou Province, Mr. Ren Zhiqing specifically proposed to build a memorial monument for him to commend his special service and encourage others. The entire Branch has passed the proposal, and a design has been drafted. Construction will begin soon in the courtyard of the Branch in Yanjiaxuan, Guiyang.

Peng Junshi, De Jingwa, Yan Yuxin, etc., did not meet with the principal. There was neither oral nor written inquiry. Only Wan Rong met with the principal, and he often told her that she had not been rehired. Wan did not ask any questions. This is the second fact that is inconsistent. The third fact that is inconsistent is that "the school's secretary, Mr. Hu, was entrusted to represent the school in court." There is no one with the surname Hu in the school's secretary. The agent entrusted by the principal was lawyer Wei Weiqing. On the day of the hearing, lawyer Wei went to Suzhou for another case and entrusted lawyer Zhang Zhu to attend the court. Mr. Hu went on to say that his administration and employment were always fair and just. None of the hired teachers were hired privately. All of them had considerable qualifications and abilities and had been approved by the Bureau of Education. The non-renewal of employment for Peng Junshi, etc., was also approved by the Bureau of Education and was a legal act. These were Mr. Hu's words. As to who is right and who is wrong, now that it has been referred to law, there shall be a proper resolution. It has now been ascertained that the former Municipal Bureau of Education and the current Bureau of Social Affairs have not received this document.

Pimping Out Daughter Prosecuted as Obstructing Morality; Daughter Does Not Wish to Sue; Court Rules Self-Prosecution Not Accepted

Tian Yang, a woman from Yangzhou residing at No. 2455 Fangbang Road in the Chinese area, is 40 years old. She had previously prostituted her daughter, Su Zhen, 15 years old, at No. 2 Yinyuli, Baxianqiao in the French Concession, at the brothel opened by Wang Xiqin (also known as Wang Linji) and his wife, Yao, together. Su Zhen is now 19 years old. Recently, Tian Yang, in her capacity as legal guardian, filed a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court, Criminal Division, in the name of her daughter, Tian Su Zhen, accusing Wang Xiqin of obstructing morality. According to the indictment, in the past, she used the excuse of recommending her daughter Su Zhen to work as a maid, luring her into prostitution, and requested a trial. The court accepted the indictment. Yesterday, Judge Chen Gongying of the Second Criminal Division summoned Tian Yang and her daughter Tian Su Zhen to the court for questioning. The defendant did not arrive. According to Su Zhen's testimony, she is 19 years old, from Nanjing, and currently resides at No. 2 Yinyuli. Yang is her mother, but she has many fathers, and she doesn't know if she is Yang's biological child. She was brought to Shanghai by Yang when she was 12 years old and was first sold for 40 yuan to work in a yarn factory for two years. Because it was difficult, she was redeemed and told to work for a company. She was deflowered when she was 15 years old and sent by her mother to work at Zai Linji's brothel. She (referring to Yang) had decided to sue the Zai Linji's owner. She does not know anything about it. She does not want to sue and wants to earn money and support her mother. Tian Yang testified that Su Zhen is her biological daughter. She does not want her to be a prostitute and wants to bring her back and find her a husband. Su Zhen then claimed that her mother sent her to be a prostitute and had written evidence. The mother signed it and took out three pledge tickets issued by Yang to the brothel owner and presented them to the court, saying that the pledge papers were not brought today. After verifying the testimonies, the court informed Tian Yang that criminal self-accusations must be made by the injured party in person, and no one else can file on their behalf. Moreover, according to Su Zhen's testimony, she does not want to sue, so the case is not established. Therefore, the court ruled that the self-accusation was not accepted. Tian Yang was dissatisfied with the verdict and left in a huff.

Tao Jingming and His Mistress Engage in Public Disputes and Legal Proceedings

Tao Jingming, 30 years old, from Pinghu, has been an employee of the Commercial Press. Three years ago, he and Wang Yueying (20 years old) began cohabitating due to their relationship. Unexpectedly, their love recently fell apart, and Wang Yueying often did not return home, each going to extremes. Yueying first published a statement attacking Tao for seducing women from good families, and Tao also published a notice in the News Daily on October 27 of this year announcing the termination of cohabitation with Wang Yueying, stating that Wang Yueying was born into prostitution and had an inherently promiscuous nature. The two sides engaged in a war of words, tit for tat, causing Wang Yueying to lose face. She then filed a lawsuit in the local court accusing Tao Jingming of defamation, obstructing freedom, and abandonment. Prosecutor Lei Binzhang ordered Tao to be released on bail after interrogation. Now the investigation has been completed, and a public prosecution has been filed, stating that anyone who can prove that the matter defamed is true shall not be punished, but this does not apply to matters involving private morality and unrelated to public interest. Article 310 of the Criminal Law has clear provisions. Whether Wang Yueying was born into prostitution or not involves private morality and cannot be publicly pointed out in the newspaper. As evidenced by the notice published in the News Daily, the defendant cannot escape the responsibility under Article 310, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. As for Wang Yueying and Tao Jingming cohabiting for many years, it is difficult to consider it as obstructing freedom. Since they were cohabiting, there is no abandonment to be discussed and should be dismissed. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Bojun interrogated Tao Jingming, who testified that he published the notice to protect his own interests because Wang Yueying first published a statement on October 23 stating that he was seducing women from good families. If he did not publish the notice, he would have acquiesced. He only cohabited with her for three years and did not marry, etc. Prosecutor Lei then presented his opinion, stating that even if Wang Yueying was a prostitute, it should not have been published in the newspapers. He requested that he be dealt with according to the law. The defendant hired lawyer Li Pengcheng for arguments and the judge adjourned the discussion and would pronounce the verdict on the 15th of this month. The defendant paid the original bail.

Guangling Tide Copyright Lawsuit

The late renowned novelist Li Hanqiu's legacy, the novel "Guangling Tide," was recently adapted into a film screenplay by Yi Hua Film Company. The film, released on the silver screen, retained the original novel's title, also naming its drama "Guangling Tide," and published advertisements for publicity. However, Zhu Rongfang, the owner of Zhenya Bookstore, which published the novel, claimed that the copyright of "Guangling Tide" had long been owned by the bookstore. Yi Hua's use of the book as the basis for its screenplay, and the identical drama title, constituted an infringement. Therefore, he engaged a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Yan Chuntang of Yi Hua in the First Special District Local Court, requesting a judgment ordering the defendant not to use the name "Guangling Tide" as a film drama title. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xu Fuji presided over the hearing. The plaintiff's attorney stated the intent of the lawsuit and presented the defendant's published advertisements as evidence. The defendant's lawyer argued that adapting a novel into a film involved a different technical process, and according to legal precedents, did not constitute infringement, and did not require the plaintiff's prior consent. After both sides concluded their arguments, Judge Xu announced that the verdict would be pronounced on the afternoon of the sixteenth of this month.

Introducing New Books

"English-Chinese Glossary of Mechanical Engineering Terms" The Chinese Mechanical Engineering Society regards the approval of mechanical engineering terms as the initial work for compiling and translating various Chinese mechanical engineering books and various mechanical engineering standards, regulations, and testing regulations. Therefore, Liu Xianzhou (currently a professor in the Department of Mechanical Engineering at National Tsinghua University), the initiator of the association, started compiling and editing. It has taken three months and has now been completed. The collected terms amount to approximately 20,000 entries, covering various commonly used terms related to mechanical engineering, such as aviation, automobiles, locomotives, power plants, and machine shops. It is truly the only reference material for those engaged in the mechanical engineering field in our country. The book is now published and sells for one yuan and fifty cents in national currency per copy. If schools and provinces purchase more than five copies at a time, they will be charged at an 80% discount. Shanghai distributors: Mechanical Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration and the Chinese Institute of Engineers at the Mainland Shopping Mall on Nanjing Road.

Miscellaneous News

Mrs. Yang's Birthday Celebration and Comfort for Soldiers On the first day of the twenty-sixth year of the Republic, it happened to be the thirtieth birthday of Mrs. Chen Hua, wife of Yang Xiaotian, commander of the Songhu Garrison. Mrs. Yang, in consideration of the hardships of the soldiers in Suiyuan fighting in the freezing cold, did not want to make a show of her birthday. All close relatives and friends who planned to send birthday gifts were requested to send cash instead, so that the total amount could be remitted to the front line to comfort the bandit suppression soldiers.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong and its surroundings are sunny, colder, and have strong northwesterly winds or gusts. The Yellow River Basin is calm and windless. The Yangtze River Basin is cloudy and foggy, gradually turning colder and showing signs of clearing, with strong northwesterly to northeasterly winds. The East China Sea and Taiwan are cloudy and rainy, with strong northwesterly to northeasterly seasonal winds. There are cyclones and rain in southern Japan, caused by a low-pressure system moving northeastward. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was 51.1 at its highest and 47.1 at its lowest. On the same day last year, the highest was 35.6 and the lowest was 29.8.

Letters

To the Editor: I have recently read the news item on page 17 of your newspaper on the 10th of this month, titled "Chinese Match Factory Workers Petitioned the Party and Government Yesterday," which involved our factory. I was very surprised to read it. It turns out that our factory, due to the old and dilapidated machinery and buildings, took advantage of the sufficient inventory and sluggish sales to suspend work at the beginning of last month in order to carry out repairs. This was a legitimate matter and was agreed to by the workers, giving them a short rest. Unexpectedly, some unscrupulous elements used this as an excuse to make demands and fabricate stories to deceive the party and government agencies. Our factory, in view of the livelihood of the workers, hurriedly completed the repairs and resumed work as usual on the 23rd of last month. This has been two weeks and there has been no unwarranted suspension of work. At present, all workers are working as usual every day. Therefore, the claim that "the workers' livelihoods are on the verge of ruin" is not true. As for the workers petitioning the party and government during the suspension period, after various agencies sent personnel to the factory to investigate, the facts have been clarified. I am deeply concerned that this may confuse the hearing, so I am writing this letter to request a factual correction. I would be deeply grateful. Sincerely, Pan Guiru, Factory Director of Shanghai China Match Factory, December 11, 25.

To the Editor: According to the representative of the Jue Lu Jiu Ji Dance Hall, after reading your newspaper on the 10th of this month, it was reported that a dancer, Shi Lian, swallowed tranquilizers in an attempt to commit suicide, which is not in line with the facts. It turns out that the dancer went to the Jue Lu Dance Hall to dance at 11:00 PM on the 4th of this month. When it was closing time, the dancer suddenly invited the dancer Chen Lili to go out with him. After Chen politely refused, the dancer roared loudly and slapped the dancer on the cheek before leaving in frustration. At about 6:00 PM on the 9th of this month, the dancer returned to the dance hall, looking angry, and insisted on inviting Chen to go out with him, threatening to commit suicide. Although the dance hall staff explained to him, he continued to mutter to himself. Observing his actions, it seemed that his nerves were suddenly stimulated, so they let him sit alone in a corner, not suspecting that he had other intentions. Unexpectedly, the dancer stubbornly took the tranquilizers he had brought with him in an attempt to commit suicide. It was regrettable. After it was discovered, the police car was immediately called to send him to the hospital for treatment. He has been cured and was discharged from the hospital that night, accompanied home by someone. He is safe and sound. Therefore, a letter was sent to the dance hall requesting that it be corrected on its behalf in order to conform to the facts. Accordingly, a representative letter is sent to your newspaper, and I hope that it will be corrected to conform to the facts. Sincerely, Lawyer Xi Wenhuan, December 11.

Women's Special Issue

Supporting Suiyuan and the Responsibility of Women

— De Lin

The current serious situation in China is the result of the encroachment and annexation by ×× imperialist powers. The outbreak of the Suiyuan Incident and the recent invasion by bandits and puppets were undoubtedly directed and instigated by its behind-the-scenes operators. Everyone knows that Suiyuan is the front line of our national defense and the barrier of the Northwest. Therefore, it is also our lifeline. For the soldiers fighting on the front line and defending our territory, in addition to cutting back on expenses, donating money, and enthusiastically transporting supplies to replenish the front-line military, fulfilling some of the obligations that citizens should fulfill, we should also give our all to the country. Although the enemy is attacking one of our provinces, its aim is to annex the entire country. The fact is very obvious. If it occupies our Suiyuan, it can control Shanxi, Ningxia, Gansu, and other provinces. Wouldn't the entire North China and Northwest fall completely into its grasp? So I say, supporting Suiyuan is supporting ourselves. We strong young people should of course make full preparations to protect our territory and complete sovereignty. However, our fellow women, who are also part of the 450 million compatriots, should unite with us, stand on the same front, and follow the example of Spanish women, who bravely defend their country for their own survival and freedom.

Spanish women not only work in the rear, but also rush to the front line to fight bloody battles. But looking back at the women in our country, they are still intoxicated in pink dreams, indulging in meaningless love affairs, and putting on makeup is a daily routine. Looking at the consumables consumed in Shanghai in the first ten months of this year, the total value of imported cosmetics and perfumes is over 1.1 million yuan. I think that in this critical moment of life and death, those aristocratic romantic lives are not needed. What is needed is a brave and active spirit, and the cultivation of habits of endurance and hard work. Look at Germany after the European War, where children went to school barefoot. In the Soviet Union after the revolution, people ate black bread. And Japanese women have the perseverance to work hard. Abyssinian women took up guns and went to the front line. Aren't these good examples for us?

Compatriots in the national women's community, please be aware! This is the critical moment of our life and death. If you have the same spirit of Spanish women bravely defending the country, at the very least, please save the money you spend on cosmetics and perfumes every day and donate it to the soldiers bravely fighting on the front line, contributing a little bit of a citizen's obligation based on your own patriotism.

My View of Modern Women

— Hu Feng

—After reading "How to Be a Modern Woman"—

In the 43rd issue of this publication, an article entitled "How to Be a Modern Woman" was published, proposing three conditions that modern women should possess: first, a sound physique; second, simple habits; and third, an independent spirit.

I believe that these three conditions are not enough for modern women. At the very least, they must also possess:

Fourth, an understanding of their own position.

The reason why women in the past would "follow the chicken if they marry a chicken, and follow the dog if they marry a dog," resulting in being poisoned by dependence, was not only due to economic dependence and lack of an independent spirit, but also because they deliberately pretended to have willow waists and golden lotuses with their very healthy bodies; they deliberately applied makeup to their faces, which contained natural beauty, to win the favor of men. All of this stemmed from economic dependence, but on the other hand, it was also because they forgot their own position and were willing to treat themselves as toys for men. This is why they were so easily bullied, played with, or looked down upon. All of these were due to a lack of understanding of their own position. We only need to see that many women in history who were able to serve the country all used the famous saying "Every man has a responsibility for the rise and fall of the country" as their creed. The reason why they had great careers to show was because they did not underestimate themselves and let men establish their achievements. In the Republic, Qiu Jin was a revolutionary martyr. She took revolution as her own responsibility, so she lived for revolution and died for revolution.

In summary, if women do not have an understanding of their own position, then I believe that the demand for women's economic independence will never succeed, no matter what. At most, it will only add some fashionable slogans in words, with no benefit to the facts. It's like modern women in China, at a time when the country is in such a critical state of survival, we should all recognize that we are also part of the 400 million people. Everyone should do their best for the country so that the country can gain equality and freedom, and then from the country's aspect, we can strive for our equality and freedom. This equality and freedom is true equality and true freedom. With true equality and true freedom, then economic independence will be truly achieved. Therefore, modern women must not lose their own position. In other words, women are also people, so people naturally have personality. I hope that modern women will recognize their own position and maintain their personality!

Reading Newspapers and Concerned People

—

The Persecution of Modern Professional Women (Part 1)

— Li Shouzhen

The day before yesterday, I went to a friend's house and talked about our respective living conditions. She complained with great indignation about the boredom of her life in recent years. She was originally a highly educated person, but annual childbirth after marriage deprived her of her health, and differences of opinion between husband and wife caused great damage to her spirit.

In order to avoid dependence and to provide for the family, she had repeatedly discussed with her husband about finding a job in society. Her husband, whom she had been in love with for five or six years before marrying, actually said to her like this: "No, this is absolutely impossible. I would rather endure the hardship of maintaining this family alone than have you seek employment. To be honest, today's society is a male-centered society. If a woman wants to get a position in society, she only needs two conditions: one is that she has already reached a shameful compromise with a man in a certain department, and the other is that a certain point of that woman—academic and talent are not included—is enough to make men want to help her. Otherwise, don't even bother to run into a wall. To put it more thoroughly, men have no one with a serious mentality towards women. If you find a job in society now, that means at least one man is harboring ill intentions towards you." When she heard this, she was furious and had a big fight with him. When she told me about it, I couldn't help but be furious!

But when we calmly think and observe, does his statement conform to the general situation today? It is true that there are women who completely create their own position with their own strength, and there are also many women who completely rely on their own labor to seek their own lives. But the situation he described is indeed not uncommon. This is the reason why the careers of women in general cannot develop today, and it is also a kind of persecution of modern professional women!

Now let's talk about the persecution that women in general suffer:

The purpose of female waitresses in ordinary tea houses and restaurants in Shanghai is to attract business. Why can they attract business by using female waitresses? The reason is very simple: "Because they are women." So what do we think is going on in the minds of their employers and those customers towards women who came to seek a legitimate job? Do they treat them as professional women with personality? Therefore, women who are determined to be independent have to suffer humiliation in order to be independent, otherwise they cannot be independent.

When business in stores is slack, they can use female shop assistants to recover. When theaters are about to close, they use ushers to attract customers. Are they promoting women's rights? Are they giving women jobs? They are only using a general shameless concept to attract a group of bored and shameless customers. What kind of persecution is this for women!

The 69-Year-Old Miss America

— Xu Jichen

I am now writing about a 69-year-old female educator. Her name is Luo Shujun. She is American and has been in China for forty years. She has never married and is a practitioner of singleness. She says: "I have lived for sixty or seventy years and have never been in love." She founded Chongzhen Girls' School in Changzhou, initially as a primary school, but now with a junior high school added. The results are remarkable, earning her widespread trust and respect from society. She is a Christian, and her entire life's work is based on God's words and deeds. Despite her "rare age," she possesses a healthy body and a sharp mind. In China, such a highly respected "old maid" is probably a rare find.

This spring, she felt that the Chongzhen Girls' School, which she had painstakingly built, was still not satisfactory. At the same time, many of the school's staff wanted to repay her for her dedication to education. Therefore, they initiated a celebration for Miss Luo's birthday, using the congratulatory gifts as an education fund. On the red invitation cards, they frankly and unceremoniously stated: "If you are willing to contribute generously, please donate in legal tender."

The scale of the event at that time was truly a sensation throughout the entire city of Changzhou. The birthday hall was set up in the school and was very magnificent. Red curtains were hung all around, and a silver statue of the God of Longevity was placed on the center table, in the same format as a Chinese birthday celebration. Five-tenths of the guests who came to offer birthday wishes were Americans, but the banquet was Chinese-style, with chopsticks, bowls, and spoons, adding a lot of laughter to the dining hall that day.

Her attitude was very sincere. She was accustomed to speaking fluent Chinese and liked to talk about her own history. Her first sentence was always: "I love China." Indeed, she regarded China as her second "motherland." When she was thirteen years old, she thought of coming to China, but her family did not allow it. She strove tirelessly to realize her "China dream." As a result, where there's a will, there's a way. Finally, at the age of twenty-eight, she arrived in China. She initially went to Songjiang and established the Bible Girls' School, making it her life's mission to save poor school-age children and preach. When she arrived in Changzhou, there were very few foreigners in the interior. As a result, some naughty children would follow Miss Luo when she ran into the street, shouting and scolding. Every day, one could hear the insults "foreign devil," "monkey," and "night ghost"!

She said: "I believe in God. God taught me to preach, God taught me to dedicate myself to education, and God taught me to endure hardship." Therefore, although she felt troubled, the light of victory and glory shone in her future, and she always showed a smiling face in the midst of trouble. Therefore, she only had the masses and forgot herself. In her forty years in China, she had no savings at all. She was a "self-made" creator. She used her brain and hands to open up a wasteland and sow seeds, which is why there is today's phenomenon of "peach and plum filling the gate." In these forty years, not only was her spirit admirable, but also her great morality and pure personality left a good impression on people.

In its early days, Chongzhen Girls' School was three simple bungalows. The location was small, the air was not well-circulated, and there were only twenty or thirty students. The only girls went to the "foreign devil's" school. However, she was not discouraged and continued to work hard. In its middle period, Chongzhen moved to a new location, three small Western-style houses, with all the necessary school equipment. The number of students also increased. Now, it has progressed from a full primary school to the addition of a junior high school. The school buildings are brand new and full of vitality! On the one hand, we celebrate her success, and on the other hand, we look forward to even greater development in the future.

We feel that how many people are willing to sacrifice themselves for society, for a certain cause, and frankly and vigorously stand up and move forward? What should women who enter social circles do?

Shen Bao Women's Special Edition Department

The Miserable Pain of Prostitutes

— Ding Xiaoru

—Thoughts on the "Death of Sai Jinhua"—

Prostitutes—the "wives" of the masses, the "mistresses" of the masses!

They dress up in "splendid clothes," they sell their "youth."

They swallow their own "sorrowful tears," only caring about others' "joy."

They regard themselves as "lambs," often subject to the "trampling" and "slaughter" of hungry tigers.

Their sense of "sex" is numb, their concept of "shame" is extinguished, but their sense of "hunger" is particularly acute.

They solve others' "sexual" hunger and thirst to solve their own hunger.

The money they earn by selling their bodies can only be used for the extravagance of the procuress, and their own lives are not even as good as a dog's.

The so-called "brightness" in their eyes is only legal tender, white rice grains, and glittering tears.

They give "loners" supreme "comfort" and "revelry."

They give people who have never known the "taste of tenderness" unlimited "tender" pleasure.

They give many satisfactions to those whose "marriages are unsatisfactory."

They can turn "miserly" people into "generous" people, and "evil" people into practitioners of "charitable" causes.

They are infected with a lot of "prosperity" and suffer all kinds of "insults."

They are truly infected with "bad diseases," ruin their bodies, and are then "cursed" for it.

They are often used as a sign of "mockery" and "abuse."

They do not know what position they occupy in society. Perhaps it is somewhere between "human" and "animal"?

But in fact, they are also "people," they are also "women" in this so-called era of "women first," the same as those praised by men.

Their end is mostly to die "coldly" in a small, dark room, naked or with only crows and magpies to peck at them, and wild dogs to drag them away. These cursed, pitiful, and also respectable (?)—special women!

Private Secretary (Part 1)

— Xueying

After Shao Yi had a big argument with her father the night before about whether or not to go abroad, Shao Wen wanted to drag her to see Brain Munshira's "Maiden's Complaint" today, but she stubbornly refused, just sitting at home listlessly by herself. Later, she was so bored that she could not stand it, so she picked up a copy of the Shen Bao for the day and read it from beginning to end. She read it very carefully, not even missing the advertisements, so she discovered a small advertisement that made her feel a little moved. The advertisement said:

"Hiring one private secretary, limited to women. Must be a graduate or student of a university liberal arts department for more than two years. Salary is ninety yuan per month for the first month, and will increase annually thereafter. Working hours are five hours per day. Please submit photos to ×× Law Firm and report for trial."

Although a monthly salary of ninety yuan is not a very large sum, it was enough for Shao Yi, a daughter from a well-to-do family who only needed to buy some clothes and pocket money, and did not have to take care of her family. But what especially pleased her was that she only needed to work five hours a day? Nowadays, the average work hours of general agencies are seven or eight hours. How could a young lady like her do it? Her father said yesterday: "Go abroad? Do you know how much money that costs? You haven't earned any money yourself, so you don't know how difficult it is to make money!" These words were very hurtful to her, so she decided to earn some money herself to show her father.

Taking photos and registering were all done surprisingly well. Later, someone sent a letter inviting her to an interview. Because she was afraid that things would not work out and turn into a joke, she boldly went alone, without even letting her sister Shao Wen know. Although the place for the interview was a lawyer's office, the person who actually interviewed her was not the lawyer. He said that he was the one hiring the private secretary, only because he was friends with the lawyer, so he borrowed his place as a correspondence address. There was no need to worry about that, but what exactly did he do? Why did he need a private secretary? And why did he have to use a female private secretary for some reason? These circumstances really should be asked carefully, but Shao Yi, who had no knowledge of the depths of society, dared to pursue her future employer in her mind like this! She allowed that guy to automatically tell her some things: his surname was Wu, he was a returned British student studying literature, and he recently wanted to run a literary publication, hoping that she could help him translate some things. The matter was decided in this way.

On the third day, Shao Yi started working. That Mr. Wu, the literary man, rented a small office in a certain building, hung up the sign of "New Moon Magazine Department," and started to compile his magazine with great pride. When Shao Yi went back on the first day after starting work, she seemed a little uneasy. First, the staff of the New Moon Magazine Department consisted of only her and that Mr. Wu, plus a child who was often sent out to do errands. Only one man and one woman were sitting opposite each other inside, and the atmosphere seemed a little different. Second, that Mr. Wu treated her too well, without any airs. Writing desks were arranged face-to-face, all the utensils were very exquisite, and there were also many fruits and expensive coffee candies prepared on a wall shelf, and he constantly and sincerely sent them over and invited her to eat. At noon, he also invited her to have Western food together, and sent a car to take her home, just like entertaining a guest. Third, not only had she not done any work herself, but that Mr. Wu had not been seen to move a pen once. This was too mysterious, and Shao Yi hardly slept all night. But the next day, there was an even more mysterious fact discovered. When she just left her house at 8:30, she saw that Mr. Wu's chauffeur was waiting outside. She naturally could not refuse, so she got in the car. This was not all. At noon, that Mr. Wu very sincerely treated her to a Chinese meal again. In the afternoon, near 4:00, that child bought two movie tickets for the balcony seats. Next was watching a movie, eating dinner, and taking a car to send her home.

A Record of the National Heroine Ms. Wa

— Junmei

Female heroes, throughout history, are too numerous to count, but those who fought for the survival of the country and the nation, besides Liang Hongyu and Qin Liangyu, who have a very glorious record, are rarely heard of. The Ms. Wa of Tianzhou mentioned here, although not as well-known as the aforementioned Liang and Qin, still leaves an indelible impression on us in the coastal areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang because of the joy of killing the enemy at that time.

During the 14th year of Jiajing in the Ming Dynasty, pirates invaded on a large scale along the southeast coast. At that time, the country had been at peace for a long time, military preparations were not in good repair, and the defending soldiers retreated at every turn, allowing them to enter the interior. The area along the Sujia Road, in particular, was ravaged, with people scattered and houses turned into ruins! It was almost occupied as a base camp. At that time, Ms. Wa of Tianzhou was known for her bravery. The court ordered her to conquer the pirates. Ms. Wa only led a thousand of her wolf soldiers and asked the way to come to help. Upon arriving, she asked the local officials to capture snakes as food. She attacked the pirates with the government army between Wangjiangjing and Beiche of Wujiang, defeating them greatly, beheading more than two thousand people. The elite of the pirates were almost completely annihilated. The corpses piled up in the fields. The wolf soldiers often dried their meat and ate it with snakes. For a time, the people were very happy. At that time, a very majestic folk song was popular: "The Hua Wa family can kill the pirates, dry and eat them like snakes." This is a song about this matter.

Special Report of this Newspaper

Dr. Su Zengxiang Discusses Women's Rights and Women's Abilities

— Jiping

With women's abilities, there will be women's rights. It is better to fight for human rights than for women's rights; only with the ability to be independent can one manage a family. In managing domestic affairs, do not forget to save the country.

The ultimate goal of the women's movement, most people always think, is to fight for "women's rights." It seems that for thousands of years, women's rights have been completely deprived by men, and now that the law stipulates equal rights for men and women, and women have the opportunity to be liberated, they should fight back for the lost women's rights. In fact, this is a prejudice, not a correct argument. Men and women are both human beings and should not be divided into different categories. Everyone should strive for "human rights." To put it more broadly, our entire Chinese nation has been subjected to the bullying and humiliation of foreign races for the past hundred years. In the face of this great disaster, we should unite to fight for the liberation and freedom of the Chinese nation. Therefore, between men and women, in addition to working together, there should be no distinction between "us" and "them." Now, many people in the women's world sympathize with this view, and Dr. Su Zengxiang is one of them. She is originally from Chongming and studied in Germany and Austria, specializing in pediatrics, and also investigated the latest childcare methods in various European countries. Last year, she returned to China. In addition to her medical practice, she also serves as a health consultant for the Modern Parents Monthly, providing free answers to various questions about children's health for parents across the country. This is an extremely important and meaningful work. The other day, I went to her clinic in Xinhuayuan, Jing'an Temple, and talked to her for a while. The following are her main opinions.

"I usually don't want to talk about this set of equal rights for men and women. I think talking about 'women's rights' out of thin air may not be effective. As long as you keep to your duty, do your best, and be practical, she will have women's rights to enjoy. To fight for 'women's rights,' you must first have 'women's abilities.' All women who have a skill are considered to have 'women's abilities,' and even handling household affairs is one of women's abilities. Once you have the 'ability,' you will have the 'right' without fighting for it; if you do not have the ability, even if you fight for the 'right,' it is only temporary and cannot be enjoyed for long. By extension, women who have the ability should seek 'human rights,' and do not need to fuss about the struggle for 'women's rights.' I once heard Hitler say, 'Women should go home!' He seemed to mean that all women should go home, which I think is too arbitrary. Some women are doing practical work in society, so are they supposed to give it up and stop doing it? These words are very necessary for certain families, but women cannot pay too much attention to social services. Doing a good job in household affairs is also as meritorious as helping the community; the ancients said, 'Cultivate your person, regulate your family, order your state, and pacify the world.' The family is the cell of social organization, so it cannot be ignored. Therefore, I advocate that men should focus on their careers, while women should focus on their families."

"Nowadays, the average woman really lacks knowledge of managing a family and raising children. I think that in girls' high schools, in addition to stipulating home economics courses, they should add basic knowledge of child health care, because single women are ultimately a minority. Since everyone is going to get married and have children, of course they need to study it. For girls who have dropped out of school, this kind of knowledge should also be taught in literacy schools; children are the masters of the future, so how can they be ignored? Based on my past medical experience, I feel that most housewives suffer both mental and physical losses due to lack of basic knowledge of family hygiene, and those responsible for education should find ways to remedy this. Second, the average lady does not have the habit of reading books or newspapers. Although they are limited by their daily work, on the one hand, it can also be said that they give up their desire for knowledge. Otherwise, no matter how busy they are, they can at least take an hour each day for self-study. I once read in a Western magazine that a mother can read five pages of a book while breastfeeding her child three months after birth, which shows their diligence in reading. If it were a Chinese housewife, she could draw a cigarette or play a game of cards while breastfeeding, which is really not necessarily a joke."

I also asked her what kind of responsibility the women's world should bear since the suppression of bandits in Suiyuan and the serious situation. She said, "With the national crisis at this point, the future situation may become even more tense. Women should work hard in the rear, for example: strengthening family responsibilities, such as inspiring children's patriotic thoughts, encouraging husbands to save the country; studying nursing and first aid; increasing knowledge of air defense and poison gas; saving family expenses and donating to national defense; participating in fundraising and comfort missions to the soldiers at the front; making clothes for the soldiers, such as gloves, earmuffs, and silk cotton vests. I am only afraid that the physique of our women's world is too poor to be able to endure hardship, and that they are used to enjoying a comfortable life and relying on maids for everything. How will they cope in wartime? In short, we must prepare as soon as possible now, so that even if disaster strikes, we will not panic. Like me personally, I have made up my mind on this. Once there is a mobilization order, I will rush to the battlefield, without hesitation, and sacrifice myself for the country, which is the most glorious end in life!"

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Not Loving the Country, But Loving the Beauty

— I

The marriage issue between King Edward VIII of England and Mrs. Simpson has been brewing for many days, causing unrest in the political situation. Only yesterday did it announce that King Edward VIII of England abdicated, and his younger brother, the Duke of York, succeeded to the throne. This issue of King Edward's marriage to Mrs. Simpson has been going on for a long time, and it can be considered that it has come to an end.

Our country originally had the famous line of not loving the country, but loving the beauty, but in our country, there are few people who can truly not love the country and love the beauty. For example, Emperor Xuanzong of Tang loved Yang Guifei very much, but by the time of the Mawei Mutiny, he had no choice but to not love the beauty and love the country. Now, King Edward VIII of England has a firm and unyielding attitude, willing to sacrifice the throne and not abandon the beauty. This attitude is not only absent in our country's history, but also unseen in the history of various countries. One cannot but say that it is the first major romance case in history.

In fact, breaking through the Eastern mirror to say, life is but a few decades, so enjoy the pleasure. For King Edward, sitting high on the throne, living in wealth and honor, to outsiders, it must be very carefree and enviable, but in the place of King Edward, he certainly does not feel any interest. England is a country with a responsible cabinet system, and the power of the monarch is very weak. Even in the case of Mrs. Simpson, he already deeply feels the pain of not being able to be free. Therefore, the King of England would rather get pleasure in spirit than get comfort in form, and would rather be somewhat wronged in form than be in pain in spirit.

As the saying goes, it is easy to find priceless treasures, but hard to find a lover, and a thousand gold pieces cannot buy a smile. If something is pleasing to me, I will spare no sacrifice to acquire it. Human nature is mostly like this, but King Edward of England is willing to sacrifice the throne rather than sacrifice the beauty. Observers often regret that the price is too great. There are many beautiful women in the world, so why bother like this? But this saying is only for those who have not fallen into the web of love. If you have already entered the web of love and want to get rid of it, it is not easy.

Therefore, I greatly feel that King Edward's firm and unyielding spirit is unattainable. He has made a solemn promise to Mrs. Simpson to marry her and will never break his promise, and he is willing to sacrifice the throne in order to fulfill his promise. In this, we can see even more that the King's personality is commendable. The throne can be abandoned like worn-out shoes, but the promise will never be broken. How can such a personality be easily found? Perhaps some people are suspicious because of Mrs. Simpson's three marriages, but this is indeed a difference in each person's vision.

Building

— Liao Chu Xiu

When I was a child, I longed for a building, a building that I could climb. There were no buildings in the rural markets. Although some things could be piled on the roof of the shops, there were no windows. Climbing in was dark and did not give people the feeling of climbing a building.

Behind my mother's back, I sometimes climbed onto the wooden ladder that leaned against the eaves. With a fearful heart, I looked around, and the crowded houses formed a sea of tiles. The setting sun smeared them into golden scales, which reminded me of the ripples of spring water reflecting the setting sun. In the sea of tiles, I could also see some trees of various kinds: the unrestrained and elegant posture of willows, the melancholy aura of loquats, especially the locust leaves, which reminded me of duckweed in the spring water.

Sometimes I looked up even higher. The clear blue sky seemed to cover the roof, and the light white clouds almost brushed my nose. So I thought of a building even more.

Without waiting for my mother to look for me, I quietly walked down the ladder. So I spent a long afternoon in the courtyard surrounded by a very high wall. I carefully searched for the small grass in the shadow of the wall, patiently adjusted the war of the ants, but I did not forget a building that could be climbed.

So I looked up again. The small white clouds flew very fast, and my heart flew with the white clouds to the sea of tiles smeared with the setting sun.

After leaving my hometown, I often lived in buildings, but I only felt the existence of "building" a few times, and that I had really climbed a building.

It was three years ago in late spring that I floated to Suzhou alone. It was already dusk when I walked up the restaurant building with travel sorrows.

The building faced west, and the setting sun cast shadows on the railing, allowing people to clearly see the passing of youth. Opposite the restaurant was a row of weeping willows, dressed in their new clothes of March, with long branches hanging straight to the ground. Because the evening mist was rising, the willow branches were especially hazy.

Leaning on the dangerous railing, I silently looked into the distance. The crimson setting sun in the willow branches was still reluctant to go down. Outside the setting sun and smoky willows, a strand of green mountains, like long eyebrows in a dream, faded into the evening mist.

A piece of market noise, along with the evening wind, swept straight over, and I began to feel that I was in a foreign land. "Don't mention other words, whose house will I stay in tonight?" I repeatedly chanted, gently patting the railing with one hand.

The setting sun finally went down, and the twilight was especially thick. I did not know where the returning team call in the nearby barracks was blowing.

The street lights flickered on, and a row of carriages flowed like water downstairs.

It was in the autumn of that year that I went alone to a small town by the river. This was not my destination, because it was raining, so I stopped halfway. There were a total of four or five hundred families in the small town. I stayed in the only tall building at the end of the market.

The rain was not heavy, but it was very even, without a break for five or six hours. Because I was going to another place tomorrow, this temporary stay brewed my travel sorrows like wine.

The small town was still a mile or two away from the riverbank, but from the building, I could see the Yangtze River. The rain was unusually hazy, making the Yangtze River a gray and white expanse. The clouds and trees across the river, which should have been seen clearly, were now a gray and black expanse.

Sometimes black sails划过江中, but because the rain was 重使得人感到十分费力, I好像觉得自己在坐在一只小船上, 在这暮雨的秋江上, 沿着江边, 由几个舟子吃力的撑着前进. 于是本来浓厚的旅愁, 就像铅块一样的压在心上。

It was hard to make the black sails cut through the river, but because the rain was solemn, it made people feel very laborious. I seemed to feel like I was sitting on a small boat, on this autumn river in the evening rain, along the river, with a few boatmen struggling to move forward. So the originally strong travel sorrows were pressed on my heart like lead blocks.

It was night, and the rain was still patiently falling. I just leaned on the building window.

The market was a piece of black, and the autumn river was also a piece of black, but I clearly felt that I was standing on a highest building, "Jinling passed through Xiaoshan Building, a traveller can be sad for one night!" I thought of whose poem.

The Flute Player

— Zhi Fu

Ping Jiugeng never enjoyed a golden childhood!

His innocent childish heart was held tightly in his father's palm. All day long, he seemed to have a great deal of unspoken bitterness left in his heart. He constantly furrowed his brow, living a very dull life.

It was spring! He could only watch groups of children tumbling and playing on the green grassland, or studying, practicing calligraphy, and singing free songs in the school next door... He always sighed and secretly reddened his eyes!

His father was an old man with a hunched back, a monkey's face, and two protruding, very fierce eyes. He also had old-fashioned tempers, which he often used to deal with his child, forbidding him from running wild and being foolish like children… If Jiugeng's legs occasionally itched, and he ran out the door, or sneaked into the school next door to listen to the sound of reading, the old man would mercilessly scold him loudly:

"Little bastard! Good-for-nothing... get in here and do your homework!"

Hearing the scolding, he would obediently sit in the dim corner, twist his neck, and practice this damned bamboo flute, less than two feet long, with a "hissing" sound, even if it was hot and he was sweating, or in the dead of winter, with his ten fingertips frozen stiff, his father would not allow him any slack.

The old man had his own experience to draw on; he said that to develop a good skill, one must temper the flute through hardship, so that he could inherit his lifetime career of being a flute player for funerals.

A year passed! Under his father's coercion, Jiugeng had memorized all the "gong che" notes thoroughly, and now he could even play "Tian Xia Tong" (1) by himself, and he was doing it quite well.

His father was naturally extremely happy! He often accompanied his flute playing, singing the upper tune (2), clapping the beat, and sometimes even excitedly jumping around on his two skinny legs.

In front of people, he often boasted about his capable child:

"Hehe! Our Jiugeng is really growing up!... You see, these days, farmers suffer so much! And the harvest is so unpredictable... That's why I'm letting my child learn this family business, so that I'll have someone to rely on in the future!..."

Often, people would express the same sentiment about his remarks: nodding, or praising the father's insightful views. - How satisfying and pleasant that was for the old man!

But this statement actually hit a wall, causing one person to express dissatisfaction. The other person was Mr. Yu, the young teacher at the village primary school.

One summer evening, while enjoying the cool air, Mr. Yu, carrying his books, said to him very seriously face-to-face in the open square in front:

"Your Jiugeng is very smart! A child like that could study for a few years, let him increase his knowledge, so that in the future..."

"Um, um! Teacher! Gotta make a living! This family business isn't easy to take over!" The old man interrupted before he could finish.

The other person sighed:

"I think that children of school age, no matter how heavily burdened by life, still need to be instilled with some knowledge..."

"...It's not like I don't know a single word, don't read a single book - and I've still managed half my life!"

The response immediately darkened his face, seeming displeased.

"The past was the society of the past! But in the future, I dare say that one cannot survive without education."

Spiritual Pivot and Basic Questions

— Answered by Dr. Liu Xinbai

Syphilis Not Fully Cured

Number 127, Ms. Wang Meijuan asks: I once suffered from syphilis and developed flat condyloma. After seeing your reply, I followed the treatment and recovered completely in a few days. Before that, I suffered from pain in my right shoulder, which was also cured by a certain doctor drawing blood, examining it, and injecting 606. (2) If the previous illness is not cured, how can I ensure a complete cure? (3) Is it necessary to continue injecting 606?

Answer: (1) Yes, it is throat syphilis. (2) Inject six doses of 606, inject 'Carbisin', test the blood once. If there is no toxin, test it again after half a year. If there is toxin, inject it as before. (3) See (2).

Is it Gonorrhea?

Number 128, Mr. Li Xishi asks: I occasionally had intercourse with a prostitute. The next day, I felt a stinging pain when urinating. Two days later, there was white pus in my urine, and the pain was unbearable. I ask (1) Is it gonorrhea? (2) What is the most effective treatment? (3) How can I prevent it from turning into syphilis or orchitis? (4) When can it be considered cured?

Answer: (1) Yes. (2) Inject ten doses of 'Sino-Acrindin', then rinse with one percent 'Argent Proteinate'. Take 'Qingzhuobian' from beginning to end without interruption. (3) Syphilis does not develop from gonorrhea, so there is no way to prevent it. With the above treatment, pay special attention to rinsing, which can avoid the danger of orchitis. (4) Please have your urine tested by a health authority. After they finish the test, they will give you a certificate. If the "Gonococcus" item on the certificate is not a plus sign (+), but a minus sign (-), then you can consider yourself cured.

Back Pain from Appendicitis

Number 129, Mr. Cheng Cheyang, No. 9, Beitiao Fang, Beitiao Road, South Chengdu Road, French Concession asks: I am twenty-one years old and live in the French Concession. Four years ago, I suffered from appendicitis. After an X-ray at the Shanghai Hygiene Sanatorium, the doctor said it was chronic appendicitis. After two months in the hospital, my body gradually returned to normal. However, my spirit could not recover, and my back still felt tired and sore. This illness has been going on for four years, and the suffering in my back has not diminished at all. Therefore, I now send this letter and humbly request your reply: (1) Is there a danger of this condition turning into something worse? (2) What is the treatment? (3) What medicine should I take?

Answer: Appendicitis is quite easy to recur. In addition, you should also be checked for kidney stones, hernias, and pyelonephritis. For appendicitis, a clinical examination is sufficient. For kidney stones and hernias, X-rays and urine tests are needed. For pyelonephritis, a test is also needed. Therefore, it is impossible to determine what disease you currently have without an examination. The treatment must wait until after a definite diagnosis.

A famous private doctor is Dr. Qu Shaoheng.

Blood in Sputum

Mr. Yu finished speaking decisively, and then looked at the father and son - Jiugeng had his head turned towards the wide open sky.

However, the old man's rigid intentions remained stubborn, and he did not feel anything about these words.

"I don't want my child to be well-read in the scriptures, more amazing than my old man!..."

After that, during the day or at night, the old man routinely supervised his child's practice of that flute, and he was even stricter than before!

The child Jiugeng, on the other hand, was like a monkey under control! Sadness occupied his chest, his life felt even more dull than before, and his brow furrowed even more tightly.

However, his innocent childish heart still maintained its original thoughts, and he did not give up his will to improve because of exploitation. During the day and night, when the bright moonlight shone on the desolate wilderness, he would often sit blankly holding the bamboo flute that his father regarded as his sole possession, leaning against the doorway, his eyes gazing at the surrounding fields, shedding tears from his eyes.

Sometimes, he would even sneak into the school next door when his father went to town, listening to the sound of people reading and those free songs!…

Note: "Tian Xia Tong": is a popular tune in the flute score. In old-fashioned weddings, that tune is used to accompany the bride and groom bowing.

Upper tune: is the jargon of the flute-playing profession, which means teaching the score.

Winter Evening

— Luo Yunhua

In the dense thicket of trees at the southwest corner of Xujiahui, he cannot see Shanghai, because he is not eyes, he can only quietly listen to the noise coming from prosperous Shanghai. Trolley car number two, continuously bringing news of bustling Shanghai, or bringing news of Xujiahui back, with its steady and rather clumsy body.

In fact, this place is lovely. In the summer, although there are many mosquitoes, the heat waves seem to be blocked by the woods. Only the long songs of the cicadas and the uniquely beautiful sound of trolley car number two linger and ripple in the calm air.

Living in this place, if nothing bothers you, or if you want to leave behind all social affairs and do some reading and writing, there is nothing better.

In the winter of 1935, because of the needs of life, such as saving on rent, I ran to that place to live. I lived in a spacious front building, facing the sun. Before I even got out of bed in the morning, or even woke up, the sunlight would warmly add a layer of weightless quilt. The light was naturally abundant, and the wind blowing from the fields, without the coal dust of the city, would gently exchange with the air in the room.

I lived this semi-rural life comfortably. Although I felt the heavy pressure of great loneliness.

Especially in early winter, like these days of not-so-cold weather, the kind of life full of village flavor, after eating dinner, gave me great interest.

Do you like to drink? It's good to drink a little to warm your heart, when you come back from the street and have been buffeted by the wind. Buy a little wine and a bag of peanuts, both are cheap and wonderful goods. You can read the evening paper while drinking. Of course, it would be best to have a close friend sitting across from you, reminiscing about funny past events, or talking about just read books or just heard things, all of which would be just great.

At that time, you can only hear the long and beautiful sounds of the tram passing by.

If there is no wind outside, along Hongqiao Road, on the way to the International Cemetery, the lights shine sparsely, and only the asphalt pavement in the middle of the road emits a firm glow. Perhaps because it is winter and it is night, the road is frozen and more solid. The sound of leather shoes passing by powerfully stirs the surrounding open fields.

Walk slowly by yourself along the neatly cultivated vegetable beds, along a hard ridge in the middle of the soft, loose soil. Sing your favorite songs in a low voice, and pour your emotions of joy and sorrow into the vast fields. They have an incomparably broad mind that can accept everything from you.

Or, just stand there and look at Shanghai, lying behind Xujiahui. At that time, I remember, once, I stood on the side of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway passing through Xujiahui, in front of me was the railway, the electric lights were weakly shining, and only a reflective rail lay horizontally on the gray ballast, like a subservient slave of non-resistance, waiting for the heavy pressure of the train. On both sides are fields and villas hidden in the thickets. Looking forward, is the frivolous and leaping city that is just starting its nightlife: the sky is burned red by the electric red lights and has become an unnatural red, as if a layer of uneven old paint has been applied to a good canvas. The lights of the cars swept over like searchlights, and the outlines of houses and trees quickly appeared and then disappeared into the darkness again. Your own face also lights up for a moment, and your eyes shyly dodge away. However, you can only see these light and shadow, you can't hear the sound, you can't even hear the sound of the tram not far away. There are only a few farmers or Tongwen College students working or walking heavily.

You or me, or anyone, standing here, seems to be isolated from the world, but there is often a feeling that Shanghai is a guy suffering from depression, and Xujiahui is still healthy. Although, if you think about it carefully, this is not very accurate.

Every night, I ran to the fields to look at the lights and shadows of the city. I didn't come back until the night wind picked up or it rained.

However, I was not able to stay there for long. Shanghai is like a magnet, and I am a piece of iron filings. The attraction of that magnet is strong, because there are my partners there, so I was attracted back and squeezed together with the iron filings.

However, I still remember the scene of these winter evenings for several months, and I send him a high degree of admiration. I hope that one day, when our cultural rest park is opened up, we will choose this lovely place so that we can enjoy the embrace of nature with peace of mind and breathe the sweet air without the smell of coal smoke.

Bao Mingshan left Shanghai last Saturday due to important matters, so Sunday's Youlian Radio piano mouth organ teaching was temporarily suspended once. He has now returned to Shanghai, and will still be teaching and playing the program announced in this newspaper last Saturday at Youlian (frequency 881) starting tomorrow at 10:30 AM.

Movies

A Further Word to Yihua Company

We are delighted that our humble and straightforward views have received a response from Yihua Film Company; at the same time, we are also disappointed because Yihua Company's response clearly does not understand our meaning.

Out of love for Yihua Company, and even more so out of love for the Chinese film industry, we presented sincere advice to Yihua Company with a fervent heart. Anyone who has read that "Respectful Announcement" letter, we believe, can see the sincerity in it. Now, this "fervent heart" has been misinterpreted as "malicious abuse," which is truly regrettable. To avoid trouble, we could have remained silent, but while it is Yihua Company's right to accept or not accept the advice of public opinion, we still have an obligation to contribute our humble opinions to the film industry. Therefore, we are still willing to offer an unnecessary response.

After "Bridal Night", what was the objective impact of Yihua Company's subsequent works on the audience? This can be "determined" by "the national film audience with a fair and impartial standpoint." At the time, we also published detailed criticisms in various newspapers, so there is no need to repeat them here. The thematic explanations of the various films listed in Yihua Company's response may seem to have sufficient reasons in writing, but the works themselves express it very clearly. The theme cannot be distorted by words. Justice resides in the hearts of the people, and facts are the most eloquent. We will leave the final judgment to the discerning audience.

We firmly believe that "producers and close friends of the heart and audience become one, and carefully create based on the needs of the audience" is the way out for Chinese films. What is meant by "becoming one with the audience" is not "flattering a small number of backward audiences, preying on their weaknesses, and catering to their preferences with various erotic and detective-like low-level interests," but rather "enriching the content while improving technical standards." Whether from a cultural standpoint or a commercial standpoint, this is an unshakeable truth. If Yihua Company believes that these opinions are all "misinterpretations and distortions," then there is naturally nothing to say; otherwise, all disputes are superfluous. As for "toilet scenery and bathroom nude shadows" being forcibly linked to "national culture," then we can only remain silent.

In short, our advice is only for the advancement of the Chinese film and cultural enterprise. We have been rigorously carrying out the work of criticism since long ago. We know that "honest advice is unpleasant to the ear, and good medicine is bitter to the mouth," but compelled by justice, we cannot betray our conscience to please others. As for distorting facts and making frivolous accusations, we only consider them shallow and ridiculous and are unwilling to argue.

Finally, we still earnestly hope that Yihua Company will henceforth respond to the criticisms of public opinion with irrefutable facts in order to achieve true victory. Signed by Thirty-Two People (names omitted)

Green Forest Song King

Showing at the Great Shanghai
